State v. McNeil


No. 37A87-4


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 657; 518 S.E.2d 486; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 880


April 13, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
August 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1997.
Writ of certiorari denied McNeil v. North Carolina, 529 U.S. 1024, 146 L. Ed. 2d 321, 120 S. Ct. 1432, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1997 (2000)
Motion granted by State v. McNeil, 565 S.E.2d 189, 2002 N.C. LEXIS 610 (N.C., 2002)
Motion granted by State v. McNeil, 605 S.E.2d 638, 2004 N.C. LEXIS 1170 (N.C., 2004)
Motion granted by State v. McNeil, 2004 N.C. LEXIS 1351 (N.C., Dec. 15, 2004)
Motion granted by State v. McNeil, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 186 (N.C., Feb. 22, 2005)
Motion granted by State v. McNeil, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 627 (N.C., June 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing sentences of death entered by Farmer, J., on 14 November 1996 in Superior Court, Wake County upon defendant's plea of guilty to two counts of first-degree murder.
State v. McNeil, 537 S.E.2d 811, 1999 N.C. LEXIS 729 (N.C., 1999)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review as of right, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), from judgments of the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina) imposing sentences of death upon his plea of guilty to two counts of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction and death sentence on two counts of first-degree murder. Appellant argued, among other contentions, that his plea agreement improperly precluded appellee State from submitting evidence of a similar murder in support of the statutory aggravating circumstance, and that the trial court erred by refusing to instruct prospective jurors to disregard parole-related considerations in determining his sentence. Appellant also argued that the trial court erred by refusing to allow him to cross-examine a witness about unserved warrants against her for felonious assault, and failed to intervene ex mero motu to preclude the prosecutor from making numerous improper statements to the jury during closing arguments. Concluding that appellant's trial and capital sentencing proceedings were free of prejudicial error, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence, holding that appellant was not prejudiced by the granting of relief that he had sought in opposing joinder of the additional murder charge. Appellant was convicted of the type of first-degree murders for which the court had previously upheld the death penalty as proportionate.


OUTCOME: Having determined that appellant's trial and capital sentencing proceedings were free of prejudicial error, the court affirmed his conviction and sentence after concluding that appellant was convicted of the type of first-degree murders for which the court had previously upheld the death penalty as proportionate.

 

2 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morganherring


No. 340A95


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 701; 517 S.E.2d 622; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 881


October 13, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
August 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied March 20, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing sentences of death entered by Hight, J., at the 10 July 1995 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Wake County, upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of two counts of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 25 February 1997.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a conviction for two counts of first-degree murder and a sentence of death from the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), alleging ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on two counts of first-degree murder and two counts of second-degree sexual offense. Upon advise of counsel, defendant pleaded guilty to the sexual offense charges. Defendant was convicted of both counts of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant alleged he received ineffective assistance of counsel because he did not understand that by pleading guilty to the sexual offense charges, he was effectively waiving any insanity defense. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence because defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding. Defendant voluntarily and knowingly entered into the plea and the court was satisfied that defendant understood the strategy behind the plea. Counsel was competent and fully believed the plea was the best way to avoid the death penalty. Based on the evidence and defendant's numerous confessions, counsel realistically concluded defendant had little defense to the charged crimes and attempted to spare his life.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of death because defendant received effective assistance of counsel at all stages of the proceedings. Defendant was fully aware of counsel's strategy in having defendant plead guilty to the sexual offense charges. Defendant knowingly and voluntarily pleaded guilty, effectively waiving an insanity defense.

 

3 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peterson


No. 328A97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 518; 516 S.E.2d 131; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 419


April 13, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 25, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Helms, J., on 12 December 1996 in Superior Court, Richmond County, upon defendant's plea of guilty to first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of an additional judgment was allowed by the Supreme Court on 14 September 1998.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Richmond County (North Carolina), which imposed a sentence of death upon defendant after defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and to robbery with a dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a grocery store, robbed the store and murdered one of the co-owners. Defendant was apprehended and arrested. Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and to robbery with a dangerous weapon. Defendant exercised his right of appeal and bypassed the Court of Appeals. Defendant maintained the instructions given to the jurors prior to voir dire were not proper, a juror was improperly dismissed, he was not permitted to give a peremptory instruction regarding mitigating factors, proper mitigating factors were not presented to the jury, and the sentence was disproportionate. The court affirmed the lower court's decision and upheld the application of the death sentence. The court reasoned that none of the issues that defendant raised on appeal created prejudicial error or resulted in an unfair sentencing proceeding. Further, the court held that the jury decided that the mitigating factors did not apply, but rather the aggravating factors of defendant's conviction of a prior violent felony and commission of murder for pecuniary gain convinced the jury. Lastly, the court held that the death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which imposed the death sentence on defendant, was affirmed because the jury properly applied the aggravating factors of defendant's commission of the murder for pecuniary gain and a prior violent felony conviction to determine that defendant should be sentenced to death.

 

4 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


No. 152A97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 411; 516 S.E.2d 106; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 424


January 12, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 25, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 246.
Writ of certiorari denied Parker v. North Carolina, 528 U.S. 1084, 120 S. Ct. 808, 145 L. Ed. 2d 681, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 246 (2000)
Related proceeding at State v. Parker, 357 N.C. 468, 587 S.E.2d 64, 2003 N.C. LEXIS 863 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Summary judgment granted by Parker v. Branker, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28911 (E.D.N.C., Mar. 31, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing sentences of death entered by Lanier (Russell J., Jr.), J., on 13 March 1997 in Superior Court, Sampson County, upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of two counts of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments was allowed 21 January 1998.
State v. Parker, 527 S.E.2d 316, 1999 N.C. LEXIS 25 (N.C., 1999)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from judgments of the Superior Court of Sampson County (North Carolina) imposing sentences of death upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of two counts of first-degree murder under the theories of felony murder and premeditation and deliberation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged judgments imposing sentences of death after he was convicted of the first-degree murders of two men. Defendant broke into a home to steal a gun. Defendant shot one of the men after he awoke while defendant was stealing the gun. The other man accosted defendant and was also killed and castrated. Defendant then set fire to the home. On the morning after the murders, defendant's family tried to have him committed and he was arrested at a detoxification center. Among numerous other contentions, defendant argued the trial court violated his rights as an indigent defendant to have two attorneys represent him while his lead attorney was ill during a pretrial proceeding; erred in failing to dismiss, at the close of all the evidence, the charge of first-degree burglary since the indictment was insufficient to allege burglary; and erred in finding that defendant's incriminating statements were entirely voluntary. The appellate court affirmed the convictions and sentences, holding that effective representation did not require that both appointed attorneys be involved in every aspect of defendant's case, and there was no error or abuse of discretion by the trial court.


OUTCOME: After finding there was no error or abuse of discretion by the trial court, the court affirmed the conviction and death sentence, concluding that the case was not substantially similar to any case in which the court had found the death penalty disproportionate because defendant was properly convicted of killing two men in their homes and showed no remorse for the brutal murders and castration.

State v. Thomas


No. 435A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 315; 514 S.E.2d 486; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 246


January 11, 1999, Heard in the Supreme Court  
May 7, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7570.
Writ of certiorari denied Thomas v. North Carolina, 528 U.S. 1006, 120 S. Ct. 503, 145 L. Ed. 2d 388, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7570 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied State v. Thomas, 355 N.C. 353, 561 S.E.2d 501, 2002 N.C. LEXIS 308 (2002)
Petition dismissed by State v. Thomas, 579 S.E.2d 573, 2003 N.C. LEXIS 371 (N.C., 2003)
Motion dismissed by State v. Thomas, 629 S.E.2d 286, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 544 (N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by State v. Thomas, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1326 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)
Motion granted by State v. Thomas, 2015 N.C. LEXIS 1327 (N.C., Nov. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Greeson, J., on 9 August 1996 in Superior Court, Guilford County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 12 May 1997.
State v. Thomas, 558 S.E.2d 193, 1998 N.C. LEXIS 784 (N.C., 1998)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), appellant challenged as of right a judgment of the Superior Court of Guilford County (North Carolina) that imposed a sentence of death on him upon a jury verdict finding him guilty of first-degree murder, robbery, burglary, and kidnapping. Appellant contended he was entitled to a new trial based on procedural and evidentiary errors by the court during his trial and capital sentencing proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his convictions for first-degree murder, contending the trial court erred by denying the motion of his two attorneys to withdraw, by failing to make necessary findings to support its initial decision to shackle him, and by abusing its discretion in refusing to unshackle him before he testified. Appellant also contended the trial court erred by denying his assignments of error pertaining to the jury selection process, claiming the prosecution was allowed to peremptorily excuse a black prospective juror on the basis of race. Appellant also asserted he was entitled to a new sentencing hearing because robbery was improperly submitted to the jury as an aggravating circumstance. The appellate court affirmed the judgment because appellant failed to satisfy the two-prong test to establish prejudicial error arising from denial of his attorneys' motions to withdraw, the reasons given by the trial court adequately explained its actions regarding appellant's restraint, the prosecution's reasons for its peremptory challenges were properly deemed race neutral, and aggravating circumstances were properly submitted to the jury.


OUTCOME: Based on its conclusion that appellant received fair trial and capital sentencing proceedings, free of prejudicial error, the court determined the sentence of death recommended by the jury and entered by the trial court must be left undisturbed because a murder committed in the home particularly shocked the conscience since such murder involved violation of an especially private place, one where a person had a right to feel secure.

State v. Anderson


No. 60A97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 152; 513 S.E.2d 296; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 239


September 29, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 9, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7210.
Writ of certiorari denied Anderson v. North Carolina, 528 U.S. 973, 145 L. Ed. 2d 326, 120 S. Ct. 417, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7210 (1999)
Later proceeding at State v. Anderson, 2003 N.C. LEXIS 135 (N.C., Feb. 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Rousseau, J., on 26 September 1996 in Superior Court, Wilkes County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to an additional judgment imposed for felonious child abuse was allowed on 22 January 1998.
State v. Anderson, 506 S.E.2d 253, 1998 N.C. LEXIS 343 (N.C., 1998)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment of the Superior Court, Wilkes County (North Carolina), which imposed a sentence of death upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant was also found guilty of felonious child abuse and sentenced to three years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Victim, a two-year old, was staying stay with defendant and her uncle. They took her to a hospital unconscious and covered with bruises, grab marks, pinch marks, scratches, bite marks, and other injuries. Victim died after life support was withdrawn. Defendant was indicted for first-degree murder and felonious child abuse. Numerous doctors testified that victim was abused. Defendant was tried capitally and found guilty of first-degree murder on the basis of malice, premeditation and deliberation; on the basis of torture; and under the felony murder rule. She was also found guilty of felonious child abuse. The jury recommended a sentence of death for the first-degree murder conviction, and the trial court entered judgment accordingly. The trial court also sentenced defendant to imprisonment for felonious child abuse. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendant received a fair capital trial and capital sentencing proceeding, free from prejudicial error, and that the imposition of the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the imposition of the death sentence because all stages of the criminal proceedings were fair and the death sentence was proportionate to the crimes she committed.

State v. Fleming


No. 175A97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 109; 512 S.E.2d 720; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 240


November 16, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 9, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Grant (Cy A.), J., on 8 April 1997 in Superior Court, Northampton County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by the Superior Court, Northampton County (North Carolina), upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to have entered the home of the victim and assaulted him with a blunt object. The cause of death was strangulation with the hand or hands. Defendant's black watch and a shoe impression matching defendant's unique shoe imprint were found at the scene of the crime. Defendant was indicted for the first-degree murder of the victim. Defendant was tried capitally and found guilty of first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation. Following a capital-sentencing proceeding, the jury recommended a sentence of death, and the trial court entered judgment accordingly. Defendant appealed on numerous grounds. The court affirmed, holding that defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding, free from prejudicial error, and that the sentence of death recommended by the jury and ordered by the trial court was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the imposition of the death penalty because the trial court committed no error during the trial or the sentencing phase and the death sentence was proportionate to the crime committed by defendant.

 

8 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 389A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 1; 510 S.E.2d 626; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 5


May 28, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
February 5, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5936.
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. North Carolina, 528 U.S. 880, 145 L. Ed. 2d 162, 120 S. Ct. 193, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5936 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williams v. State, 2003 N.C. LEXIS 742 (N.C., June 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Manning, J., on 23 July 1996 in Superior Court, Bertie County, upon defendant's plea of guilty to first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 13 October 1997.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to bypass the Court of Appeals and sought review of a decision from the Superior Court, Bertie County (North Carolina), which imposed the death sentence after defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raped and murdered an 83-year-old woman. Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder and other related charges. He was convicted and received the death penalty. Defendant sought review and argued that the trial court committed multiple errors. He argued that the trial court erroneously admitted details of his prior criminal activity; that the trial court erred when it submitted mitigating circumstances to the jury; that the defendant received ineffective assistance of counsel; and that the trial court erred when it admitted photographic evidence of the victim's condition after the attack. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. It found that the prior criminal activity was properly admitted, that it was proper to submit the mitigating circumstances to the jury, that the defendant's counsel's performance did not fall below an object standard of reasonableness, and that it was proper to admit photographic evidence of the victim's condition after the murder because the Rules of Evidence did not apply in a sentencing hearing. The court conducted a proportionality review and found that defendant's punishment was proportionate to that of similarly situated defendants.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence because it found that the trial court did not commit errors during the sentencing hearing, that defendant received effective assistance of counsel, and that the sentence was proportionate to the sentences received by other similarly situated defendants.

 

9 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Malette


No. 79PA98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


350 N.C. 52; 509 S.E.2d 776; 1999 N.C. LEXIS 12


October 14, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
February 5, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal of a substantial constitutional question pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) and on discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of a per curiam, unpublished decision of the Court of Appeals, 128 N.C. App. 749, 496 S.E.2d 850 (1998), affirming an order and supplemental order entered by Hudson, J., at the 18 March 1996 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Durham County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the North Carolina Court of Appeals decision that held N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-534.1(b) was constitutionally applied after a post-detention hearing was held following defendant's arrest on a domestic violence warrant and a secured bond set.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged an appeals court decision that held N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-534.1(b) was constitutionally applied to defendant after his arrest on a domestic violence warrant. The state supreme court affirmed the decision of the appeals court. Defendant's fundamental liberty rights were not violated, as there was no unreasonable delay in receiving a prompt post-detention hearing before the first available judge. Defendant received a post-dentition hearing the day after his arrest where a secured bond amount was set.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed an appeals court decision that held a state statute covering bail conditions and pretrial release for individuals accused of domestic violence crimes was constitutionally applied to defendant after his arrest on domestic violence charges. There was no indication that unreasonable delay in holding a post-detention hearing occurred as defendant received a hearing the day after his arrest where bond was set.

 

10 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Meads v. North Carolina Dep't of Agric., Food & Drug Protection Div., Pesticide Sec. (In re Pesticide Bd. File Nos. IR94-128, IR94-151, IR94-155)


No. 139A98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


349 N.C. 656; 509 S.E.2d 165; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 844


November 18, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by respondent pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(2) of an unpublished decision of a divided panel of the Court of Appeals, 128 N.C. App. 750, 498 S.E.2d 210 (1998), affirming an order entered by Farmer, J., on 7 February 1997 in Superior Court, Wake County. On 8 July 1998, the Supreme Court allowed petitioner's petition for discretionary review of additional issues.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent North Carolina Department of Agriculture, Food and Drug Protection Division, Pesticide Section (NCDA) sought review of the decision of the court of appeals (North Carolina) which affirmed the trial court's reversal of the decision of the NCDA which found that petitioner sprayer violated N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 143-443(b), 143-469(b)(2), 143-456(a)(2), (4), and (5), and North Carolina Admin. Code tit. 2, r. 9L .1005(b), (c), and (e).


OVERVIEW: The sprayer aerially sprayed pesticide on the farmer's soybean field. A neighbor exited her home and encountered a vapor that made her eyes burn and her lips tingle. The neighbor complained to the NCDA. The Pesticide Board concluded that the sprayer violated laws by applying the pesticide in a manner inconsistent with its label and by applying it in a faulty, careless, or negligent manner. The Pesticide Board concluded that the sprayer also aerially deposited pesticide within 300 feet of the nearby business, 25 feet of a highway, and 100 feet of the neighbor's residence. The sprayer sought judicial review in the trial court. The trial court reversed. The court of appeals affirmed and the court reversed. The court held that the court of appeals erred in holding that there was not substantial evidence to support the pesticide board's decision to assess a civil penalty. The court concluded that rule 9L .1005 did not violate the constitutional rights of due process or equal protection. The distinction between aerial and ground applicators was rationally related to the increased likelihood of an off-target occurrence associated with aerial application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and reinstated the NCDA's decision against the sprayer.

 

11 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Call


No. 341A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


349 N.C. 382; 508 S.E.2d 496; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 848


May 28, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Rousseau, J., on 23 July 1996 in Superior Court, Ashe County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his appeal of additional judgments was allowed by the Supreme Court on 2 September 1997.



DISPOSITION: FIRST-DEGREE MURDER: NO ERROR IN GUILT-INNOCENCE PHASE; DEATH SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR NEW CAPITAL SENTENCING PROCEEDING. ROBBERY WITH A DANGEROUS WEAPON: NO ERROR. FIRST-DEGREE KIDNAPPING: NO ERROR. ASSAULT WITH A DEADLY WEAPON WITH INTENT TO KILL INFLICTING SERIOUS INJURY: JUDGMENT ARRESTED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Ashe County (North Carolina), convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant was also found guilty of robbery with a dangerous weapon, first degree kidnapping, and assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury. Defendant appealed, and his motion to bypass the appellate court was allowed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged several aspects of the pretrial proceedings, jury-selection phase, guilt-innocence phase, and the capital sentencing proceeding. The court held that: (1) defendant was unable to show that he was prejudiced by an alternate juror who did not deliberate either defendant's guilt or sentencing; (2) that defendant failed to show that his presence at an unrecorded bench conference would have been useful; (3) that defendant was unable to establish a prima facie case of gender discrimination in the jury selection process; (4) that the handwritten note admitted into evidence was not a confidential communication protected by the spousal privilege; (5) that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's convictions; (6) that it was not grossly improper for the prosecution to use photographs during closing arguments or at the capital sentencing; (7) that the indictment charging defendant with assault with a deadly weapon was fatally flawed because it failed to list the proper victim; and (8) that the prosecutor misspoke during the capital sentencing in regard to defendant's silence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for first degree murder, kidnapping, and robbery with a dangerous weapon was affirmed. The court arrested judgment as to defendant's conviction for assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings. Defendant's death sentence was vacated and also remanded for a new capital sentencing proceeding.

 

12 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Murillo


No. 209A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


349 N.C. 573; 509 S.E.2d 752; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 851


September 30, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 31, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5310.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Ellis, J., on 18 April 1996 in Superior Court, Richmond County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from the judgment of the Superior Court, Richmond County (North Carolina), which imposed a sentence of death upon defendant following a jury verdict finding him guilty of first-degree murder of his wife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was abusive to his wife for several years, and she died of a gunshot through the temple. At trial, the state brought evidence of abuse from several sources, which was admitted over defendant's objections to show state of mind. The jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder and he was sentenced to death. On appeal of right, the court found that evidence of abuse was admissible under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 401, because it was relevant and its probative value outweighed any prejudice to defendant. The court found that the trial court had properly admitted under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 404(b) evidence of defendant's guilty plea to involuntary manslaughter in California 22 years before for the similar death of his first wife. The court noted that the scope of cross-examination was within the discretion of the trial court. The court found no jury misconduct, and found that the state's closing argument was not prejudicial to defendant because it was proper to discuss aggravating circumstances under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(e)(3). The court held that the sentence was proportionate and that there was no error in the trial or the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no error in the judgment, which imposed a sentence of death upon defendant after the jury found him guilty of first-degree murder in the death of his wife. The court found that there was no prejudicial error when the trial court admitted evidence of defendant's guilty plea to involuntary manslaughter of his first wife, and that the sentence was proportionate.

 

13 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. 80PA98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


349 N.C. 483; 508 S.E.2d 277; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 846


October 14, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal of a substantial constitutional question pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) and on discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 128 N.C. App. 547, 496 S.E.2d 597 (1998), affirming an order and supplemental order entered by Hudson, J., at the 18 March 1996 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Durham County.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, arrested on charges of domestic assault, challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which affirmed the lower court's decision that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-534.1(b), by which defendant was detained, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for on charges of domestic assault and was detained pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-534.1(b), which authorized a magistrate to detain defendant in jail for 48 hours prior to trial and without a prompt post-detention hearing before a judge. Defendant moved to dismiss the charges against him under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-954(a)(4), alleging that the detention statute was unconstitutional. The district court dismissed the charges. The state appealed and the reviewing court affirmed. Defendant appealed, contending that § 15A-534.1(b) was unconstitutional facially and as applied in his case. The court held that the statute was facially constitutional. However, the court determined that application of § 15A-534.1(b) significantly harmed defendant's fundamental right to liberty when unreasonable delay prevented him from receiving a prompt post-determination hearing before the first available judge regarding the conditions of his pretrial release. The court held that defendant was not given an opportunity to be heard at a meaningful time and in a meaningful manner, and the application of § 15A-534.1(b) violated his procedural due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision upholding the constitutionality of the state statute under which defendant was detained, and remanded for the entry of an order of dismissal.

 

14 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 61A98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


349 N.C. 332; 507 S.E.2d 28; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 726


October 1, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 4, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review prior to determination by the Court of Appeals, granted by the Supreme Court ex mero motu pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31(a) and Rule 15(e)(2) of the North Carolina Rules of Appellate Procedure, of orders entered 23 May 1997 and 11 June 1997 by Manning, J., in Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, class of taxpayers, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), which decertified the class and dismissed the class' action for refunds of the intangibles tax, in favor of defendants, State and Secretary of Revenue (Secretary).


OVERVIEW: The class challenged the constitutionality of the intangibles tax levied under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-203. The class was composed of taxpayers who paid the intangibles tax but failed to meet the notice requirements of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267. Under the tax scheme of N.C Gen. Stat. § 105-203, shareholders of corporations doing business inside the state were taxed at a lower rate than shareholders of corporations not doing business within the state. Subsequently, the Supreme Court held that the deduction provision was unconstitutional. The trial court decertified the class and dismissed the action for refunds for failure to comply with N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267. In response to the Supreme Court's decision, 1997 N.C. Sess. Laws 771,771 was enacted, which based the refund rights of the class on the notice requirements N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267. The court reversed the decision of the trial court because all the taxpayers who benefited from the unconstitutional deduction provision were relieved of liability. Further, taxpayers complying with §105-267 were provided a refund. Thus, 1997 N.C. Sess. Laws 771,771, violated the tax uniformity requirement of N.C. Const. art. V, § 2(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, which dismiss the tax refund claims of the class.

 

15 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Polaroid Corp. v. Offerman


No. 70PA98


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


349 N.C. 290; 507 S.E.2d 284; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 727


October 12, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 4, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied May 3, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3039.


PRIOR HISTORY: On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 128 N.C. App. 422, 496 S.E.2d 399 (1998), reversing an order entered by Cashwell, J., on 28 February 1997 in Superior Court, Wake County, and remanding for entry of summary judgment for plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Secretary of Revenue of the State of North Carolina (secretary), sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which reversed a trial court and granted summary judgment in favor of appellee taxpayer in the taxpayer's action that sought a refund of taxes paid.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer received a judgment in a patent infringement action and classified the judgment for North Carolina corporate income tax purposes as nonbusiness income under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-130.4(a)(1). Thus, the judgment was allocated to Massachusetts, the state of its commercial domicile. The North Carolina Department of Revenue reclassified the award as business income which increased the taxpayer's tax liability. The secretary upheld the department's decision and the taxpayer paid the tax due and sought a refund. The trial court granted the secretary's motion for summary judgment and the appellate court reversed the trial court and granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer. The court reversed the appellate court and held that § 105-130.4(a)(1) encompassed the independent functional test which allowed extraordinary transactions to constitute business income if the relevant asset was used by the corporation in its regular course of business. The judgment compensated the taxpayer for infringement of its patents which were an integral part of its regular business, and thus the court held the judgment constituted income and should have been classified as business income.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court and entered summary judgment in favor of the secretary in the taxpayer's action that sought a refund of taxes paid.

State v. Davis

SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA

DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Buncombe County (North Carolina), convicted defendant of three counts of first-degree murder, one count of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury, and one count of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the murder convictions and to consecutive prison sentences for the assault convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was terminated from his employment following an altercation with a fellow employee. Two days later he entered the employer's premises with a rifle and a handgun and began systematically firing both weapons into management offices. Three people died and two were wounded. Bethania Town Lot Comm. v. City of Winston-Salem


No. 402PA97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 664; 502 S.E.2d 360; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 363


February 12, 1998, Heard in the Supreme Court  
July 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 and on appeal of right of a constitutional question pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) to review a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 126 N.C. App. 783, 486 S.E.2d 729 (1997), vacating an order granting a permanent injunction entered by Burke, J., at the 10 June 1996 Civil Session of Superior Court, Forsyth County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, town lot committee and others, appealed the judgment from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which upheld the validity of 1995 N.C. Sess. Laws 74 that established the town of Bethania that consisted in size of 400 acres.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed that the town of Bethania was created by the general assembly in 1839 and comprised 2,500 acres. Defendants, city and others, claimed that the town of Bethania was not created by the 1839 Act of the general assembly because there were no records showing that the inhabitants of the town ratified the 1839 Act. Defendants claimed that the town of Bethania was created by 1995 Sess. Laws 74 (1995 Act) and consisted of 400 acres. The court noted that the general assembly had the authority, by special or local act, to create municipalities and change the boundaries of municipalities. The court found that this caused plaintiffs' argument that the 1995 Act violated certain parts of the North Carolina Constitution to fail. The court found that the North Carolina Constitution did not direct the general assembly to create municipalities by general laws. Plaintiffs also contended that the 1995 Act violated N.C. Const. art. II, § 24(2). This section provided that the general assembly could not enact a prohibited local act by the partial repeal of a general law. The court held that the 1995 Act was not a prohibited local act and affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court that found that the town of Bethania was created in 1995 by the general assembly.

State v. Green


No. 519A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 588; 502 S.E.2d 819; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 364


September 11, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
July 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied January 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 692.
Writ of certiorari denied Green v. North Carolina, 525 U.S. 1111, 142 L. Ed. 2d 783, 119 S. Ct. 883, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 692 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: On review of a substantial constitutional question, pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1), of a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 124 N.C. App. 269, 477 S.E.2d 182 (1996), affirming judgments entered upon defendant's convictions of first-degree sexual offense, attempted first-degree rape, and first-degree burglary by Cashwell, J., on 26 January 1995 in Superior Court, Wake County.
State v. Green, 124 N.C. App. 269, 477 S.E.2d 182, 1996 N.C. App. LEXIS 1055 (1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which dismissed defendant's claims of constitutional error in defendant's transfer, trial and sentence as an adult of first-degree rape, first-degree burglary and first-degree sexual offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was convicted and sentenced as an adult of first-degree rape, burglary, and sexual offense. The appellate court dismissed defendant's appeal of constitutional error related to the transfer from juvenile court to the trial court. On appeal, the court did not find any merit in defendant's contention that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-710 violated his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. V, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.C. Const. art. I, § 19. Section 7A-710 was not void for vagueness and provided sufficient guidance to the juvenile court judges in making their transfer decisions. Next, the court also rejected the contention that defendant's sentence of life imprisonment constituted cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.C. Const. art. I, § 27. The court concluded that defendant sentence was within the bounds of society's current and evolving standards of decency, was not grossly disproportionate to the crime he committed, and was not totally without penological justification. The court affirmed the dismissal of the appeal and affirmed defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, which dismissed defendant juvenile's petition for a writ of mandamus, because defendant's due process rights were not violated and defendant's sentence to a term of life imprisonment was not cruel and unusual punishment.

Smith Chapel Baptist Church v. City of Durham


No. 250PA97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 632; 502 S.E.2d 364; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 362


November 19, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
July 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31, prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals, of a judgment entered by Manning, J., on 11 October 1996 and an amended judgment entered on 3 January 1997 in Superior Court, Durham County.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of plaintiff landowner, which found that the city did not have authority to assess fees to operate its stormwater program.


OVERVIEW: The city assessed the landowner fees to operate its stormwater program. The landowner brought an action against the city. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the landowner. The court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed. The court stated that N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 160A-311, 160A-314(a1), did not alone authorize the city to collect fees for the stormwater program. The court stated that N.C. Const. art. XIV, § 5, gave the city the authority to regulate the water therefore it had supplementary power to carry the stormwater program into effect. The court stated that the city was authorized by statute to use the impervious-area method in setting the fees and that there was substantial evidence that this was the best method for calculating the fees. The court stated that it was not arbitrary and capricious for those who caused the problem to pay for the stormwater plan.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the landowner. The court found that the city had the authority to assess fees to operate its stormwater program.

Bring v. North Carolina State Bar


No. 355PA97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 655; 501 S.E.2d 907; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 365


December 18, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
July 30, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Bring v. North Carolina State Bar, 349 N.C. 242, 514 S.E.2d 271, 1998 N.C. LEXIS 650 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 and on appeal of right of a constitutional question pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) to review a decision of the Court of Appeals, 126 N.C. App. 655, 486 S.E.2d 236 (1997), affirming an order entered by Spencer, J., on 4 June 1996 in Superior Court, Wake County.
Bring v. North Carolina State Bar, 126 N.C. App. 655, 486 S.E.2d 236, 1997 N.C. App. LEXIS 598 (1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner law school graduate appealed an order from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina) that affirmed the trial court's affirmance of a bar council's refusal to approve her law school so that she could sit for the bar examination.


OVERVIEW: The student graduated from a law school that was not accredited by the state and she was not allowed to sit for the bar exam. The student alleged that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 84-24, which governed the rules for bar admission, violated the state constitution because it delegated legislative power to the Board of Law Examiners (board) without adequate standards to control its action. The trial and appellate court upheld the board's decision. On appeal, the state supreme court held that the statute's legislative goals and policies, combined with its adopting rules and regulations, were sufficient to withstand such a challenge. The court found that there was a need for expertise in the achievement of the legislative policy and that the board was more suited to making a decision such as this than was the legislature. Further, there were adequate procedural safeguards to assure adherence to legislative standards because a council and the court were required to approve the board's rules. The court ruled that the board's rule was properly adopted and that the board was not required to adopt the rules according to the Administrative Procedure Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

State v. Lemons

SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA

July 9, 1998, Filed

Osmond, III), J., on 18 August 1995 in Superior Court, Wayne County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments for two counts each of first-degree kidnapping and robbery with a firearm was allowed 17 July 1997.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from two judgments imposing sentences of death entered by the Superior Court, Wayne County (North Carolina), upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others convicted of murder in two fatal shootings were arrested after he assaulted a victim with the murder weapon. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erred by admitting evidence of the unrelated assault. Specifically, defendant contended that the trial court erred by admitting (1) the victim's testimony regarding the assault, (2) the testimony of three law enforcement officers concerning the investigation of that incident, and (3) eight photographs of the victim's injuries and the crime scene. The crux of defendant's argument appeared to be that even if admissible under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 404(b), evidence of the prior assault should have been excluded under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 8C-1, N.C. R. Evid. 403 (1992). The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting evidence of misconduct otherwise admissible under Rule 404(b). In fact, the trial court guarded against the possibility of prejudice by providing the jury with a limiting instruction before the victim's testimony. The court further concluded that defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding, free from prejudicial error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first-degree murder and the death sentences imposed.

State v. Warren


No. 116A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 80; 499 S.E.2d 431; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 216


October 15, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
May 8, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6278.
Writ of certiorari denied Warren v. North Carolina, 525 U.S. 915, 119 S. Ct. 263, 142 L. Ed. 2d 216, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6278 (1998)
Writ denied by State v. Warren, 359 N.C. 286, 610 S.E.2d 714, 2005 N.C. LEXIS 31 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Warren v. Polk, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7871 (M.D.N.C., Jan. 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Greeson, J., at the 18 March 1996 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Guilford County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Guilford County (North Carolina), which convicted him of first degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(e)(2) after he confessed to the subject murder and several others and conceded guilt to second degree murder in penalty phase closing arguments. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress his confession on Fifth and Sixth Amendment grounds. On appeal, the court held that the Sixth Amendment right had not attached to this murder, but only to other murders he had committed because at that time defendant had not yet committed this murder. Similarly, defendant's Fifth Amendment rights were not violated because there was a break in custody between his assertion and his confession. Excusal of a potential juror was proper where she admitted her inability to vote for the death penalty. The § 15A-2000(e)(2) aggravating circumstance language was properly submitted to the jury despite the fact that his other first degree murder convictions came after this one because he committed those murders before this one and was convicted for them before the sentencing proceeding for this one.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that defendant received a fair trial free from prejudicial error and that the sentence of death imposed by the trial court was not excessive or disproportionate.

Bailey v. State


No. 53PA96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 130; 500 S.E.2d 54; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 214


September 12, 1996, Heard in the Supreme Court  
May 8, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals from an order for plaintiffs entered by Thompson, J., on 2 June 1995 and an amended order entered on 25 September 1995 in Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a state, the state Department of Revenue, the secretary of the state Department of Revenue, Department of State Treasurer, and state treasurer challenged the decision of the Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina), which held that legislation that partially taxed state and local government retirement benefits was an unconstitutional impairment of contract, a material breach of contract, and an unconstitutional retroactive tax.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the relationship between the public employee retirement systems and plaintiff state and local government employees whose retirement benefits vested was contractual in nature, that the right to benefits exempt from state taxation was a term of such contract, and that such exemption did not constitute an unconstitutional contracting away of the state's taxation power. The state's passage of 1989 N.C. Sess. Laws chapter 792, § 3.9 (the Act), which placed a cap on the amount of benefits exempted from state taxation, impaired the contract and the impairment was not reasonable and necessary to serve an important public purpose. Thus, the Act was an impermissible impairment of contract under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The Act also constituted an unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation. The court held that the trial court's error in granting an injunction barring future collection of taxes was not prejudicial and that the state should cease collection of taxes pursuant and begin issuance of refunds. The court held that the trial court erred by limiting relief only to those taxpayers who protested in accordance with N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-267 (1989).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding that legislation that partially taxed state and local government retirement benefits was unconstitutional as an improper impairment of contract and a taking of property without just compensation and affirmed the creation of a common fund for payment of attorney fees. The court remanded for entry of orders with respect to the determination and administration of the employees' class, refunds, and the common fund.

In re Appeal of Springmoor, Inc.


No. 79PA97


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


348 N.C. 1; 498 S.E.2d 177; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 153


October 14, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 3, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of Wake County pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) from a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 125 N.C. App. 184, 479 S.E.2d 795 (1997), reversing an order of the Property Tax Commission entered 16 November 1995 and holding N.C.G.S. § 105-275(32) unconstitutional in part. On 5 June 1997, the Supreme Court allowed discretionary review of an additional issue.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgment from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), that found that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32)(v) violated the prohibition against the establishment of religion found in N.C. Const. art. I, § 13 and U.S. Const. amend. I, as applied to the states through U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The issue presented on appeal was whether N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32)(v) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Following the judgment that held that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32)(v) violated the prohibition against the establishment of religion found in the state and federal constitutions, appellant county sought review. The issues raised were whether N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32)(v) was unconstitutional and, if so, whether the allegedly unconstitutional N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32)(v) could be severed, allowing the remainder of the statute to stand. The court affirmed in part, holding that the tax benefit bestowed on religious entities by § 105-275(32)(v) was not merely incidental, but rather was an exclusive benefit denied to other similarly situated nonprofit homes for the aged. The court reasoned that to differentiate between the homes resulted in the favoring of the religious over the secular. Additionally, the court reversed in part because § 105-275(32)(v) was an integral part of the definition of a qualifying home for the aged, sick, or infirm contained in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 105-275(32) and could not be severed. The court concluded that the court of appeals erred in severing.


OUTCOME: The judgment that found that the statute pertaining to property classified and excluded from taxes violated the prohibition against the establishment of religion was affirmed in part because the tax benefit bestowed by the statute was an exclusive benefit denied to other similarly situated nonprofit homes for the aged. The judgment was reversed in part because the court of appeals erred in severing a portion of the statute.

State v. Smith


No. 233A96


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


347 N.C. 453; 496 S.E.2d 357; 1998 N.C. LEXIS 12



February 6, 1998, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Downs, J., at the 22 April 1996 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Buncombe County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments imposed for first-degree arson, conspiracy to commit first-degree arson, two counts of attempted first-degree murder, misdemeanor larceny, and credit card fraud was allowed 17 July 1997.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a jury verdict of guilty on the first-degree murder charge and the sentence of death entered in the Criminal Session of Superior Court, Buncombe County (North Carolina). He was also convicted of two counts of attempted first degree murder, first degree arson, conspiracy to commit arson, larceny, and credit card fraud. He claimed prejudicial error by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole mail from an apartment building, including a credit card bill the card number of which he used to order clothing from a catalog. He decided that he could be connected to the mail theft and decided to destroy the evidence by setting fire to the apartment building. Defendant and a companion used kerosene they purchased to ignite a fire in the apartment building. One man died from smoke inhalation and two women were severely injured. At the guilt/innocence phase of his trial on charges of first degree murder and attempted first degree murder, he presented no evidence. He was convicted of all charges. At the sentencing phase he was received the death penalty. On appeal, the court concluded that there was no error by the trial court in (1) failing to permit defendant to voir dire the jurors on the issue of parole, (2) admitting his medical records from the jail, (3) the state's peremptory strike of one black prospective juror, (4) refusing to instruct the jury as to second degree murder, (5) failing to intervene ex mero motu to correct allegedly improper arguments by the state, or (6) submitting aggravating and mitigating circumstances in the penalty phase.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that defendant received a fair trial, free from prejudicial error, on the charge of first degree murder and a fair capital sentencing proceeding. It further concluded after conducting a proportionality review of the sentence that the sentence of death was not excessive or disproportionate.

Lynn), J., on 1 June 1995 in Superior Court, Cumberland County, upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of three counts of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to an additional judgment was allowed 3 July 1996.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7a-27(a) from the judgment of the Superior Court of Cumberland County (North Carolina), which entered conviction on three counts of first-degree murder and imposed three sentences of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty on three counts of first-degree murder and sentenced to death for each of the three murders. The court held that defendant's conviction and sentence were proper. The court held: (1) the trial court properly excused for cause two prospective jurors; (2) the trial court properly denied defendant's for-cause challenge of a juror who stated that she could fairly consider the sentencing alternatives; (3) defendant's first-degree rape conviction properly supported his conviction for the first-degree murder of the adult victim under the felony murder theory; (4) defendant failed to make the necessary showing that by his intoxication he was utterly incapable of forming the requisite intent for murder; (5) the trial court properly instructed the jury on malice, specific intent, premeditation, and deliberation in its first-degree murder instructions; (6) the record supported the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances; (7) the death penalty was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor; and (8) the death sentence was not disproportionate and defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and imposition of the death sentences.

State v. Stephens

Related proceeding at State v. Stephens, 553 S.E.2d 684, 2001 N.C. LEXIS 960 (N.C., 2001)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Stephens v. Branker, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 73788 (E.D.N.C., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing three sentences of death entered by Cashwell, J., at the 27 November 1995 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Johnston County, upon jury verdicts finding defendant guilty of three counts of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments was allowed by this Court 19 December 1996.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged judgment of conviction for three counts of first degree murder and three counts of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury by the Superior Court, Johnston County, North Carolina.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to defendant's conviction for three counts of first-degree murder and three counts of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury, he argued that the trial court erred in instructing the jurors, in the sentencing phase, that they were required to consider only statutory mitigating circumstances that they deemed to have mitigating value. The court found that the jurors were not so misled and defendant was not entitled to a new sentencing hearing. The court found that reading the entire jury charge in context, the instructions in question could not have had the effect of confusing issues of statutory and nonstatutory mitigating circumstances for the jury. Furthermore the court held that a mere lapse in language by the trial court while reading instructions to the jury, which was not called to the trial court's attention at the time it was made, would not have constituted prejudicial error when it was apparent from the contextual reading that the jury could not have been mislead. Furthermore, the court found that the sentences of death imposed upon defendant were not disproportionate to the crimes committed.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial court's judgment of conviction entered against defendant. Specifically, the court found that the jury charge regarding statutory and nonstatutory mitigating circumstances did not constitute prejudicial error and the death sentences imposed were not disproportionate to the crimes committed.

State v. Gray


No. 556A93


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


347 N.C. 143; 491 S.E.2d 538; 1997 N.C. LEXIS 655


April 8, 1996, Heard in the Supreme Court  
October 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Wright, J., at the 1 November 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Lenoir County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for first-degree murder and a judgment imposing a sentence of death, from the Superior Court, Lenoir County (North Carolina). Defendant made 29 assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death following a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder of his wife. The court overruled all 29 assignments of error finding no error in the trial or sentencing proceeding and held that the death sentence was proportionate. There was no error in the trial court's refusal to charge on self-defense because all of the evidence that would exculpate defendant showed that a shooting by his wife was accidental. There was no error in the admission into evidence during the sentencing hearing of four misdemeanor warrants against defendant. The wife had sworn to the warrants and evidence contained on the warrants was probative of an aggravating circumstance that defendant killed a witness against him. There was no error in the denial of defendant's motion to suppress all his statements to law enforcement officers and items gathered in a search of his home. Police had probable cause to arrest defendant after a neighbor told that he had killed his wife. When defendant came to the door armed with a toy pistol, this was an exigent circumstance that justified the police officers entering the house without a search warrant to arrest defendant.


OUTCOME: The court found no error in the trial or sentencing proceeding and held that the death sentence was not disproportionate. The evidence supported the findings of aggravating and mitigating circumstances and the sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. Defendant did not try to help the victim, he did not confess, and the transcript reflected evidence of numerous motives for the murder.

State v. Flowers


No. 553A94


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


347 N.C. 1; 489 S.E.2d 391; 1997 N.C. LEXIS 597


November 12, 1996, Heard in the Supreme Court  
September 5, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended September 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Stephens (Ronald L.), J., at the 19 September 1994 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Rowan County. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to an additional conviction was allowed by this Court 22 April 1996.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded to the Superior Court, Rowan County, for a new sentencing hearing on the conspiracy conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to commit murder and first-degree murder. Following a capital sentencing proceeding pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000, the jury recommended the death sentence for the murder conviction. The Superior Court of Rowan County (North Carolina) sentenced defendant to death for the first-degree murder conviction and to a term of 10 years for the conspiracy conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous assignments of error concerning both the guilt/innocent phases and sentencing phases on both charges. On appeal, the court found that the superior court had not erred in conducting the trials and affirmed the judgments of conviction. The court also affirmed the imposition of the death penalty on the first-degree murder charge. However, the court found that the superior court erred by imposing a sentence in excess of the presumptive sentence for conspiracy to commit murder without making findings in aggravation as required by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1340.4(a). The court reasoned that since the presumptive sentence for the conspiracy charge was three years, the superior court was required to find and weigh the aggravating and mitigating factors before it imposed a sentence greater than that contained in the statute. Accordingly, that portion of the judgment was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction and of sentence on the first-degree murder charge were affirmed. The judgment of conviction on the conspiracy to commit murder charge was affirmed, however, the judgment of sentence on that charge was vacated and remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

State v. Strickland

SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA

July 24, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Strickland v. North Carolina, 522 U.S. 1078, 118 S. Ct. 858, 139 L. Ed. 2d 757, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 524 (1998)
Related proceeding at State v. Strickland, 354 N.C. 579, 559 S.E.2d 551, 2001 N.C. LEXIS 1256 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Stay denied by, Motion granted by, Summary judgment granted by Strickland v. Lee, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 6743 (W.D.N.C., Jan. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Steelman, J., on 26 October 1995 in Superior Court, Union County, upon a jury verdict of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court, Union County (North Carolina), for first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation. In a separate capital sentencing proceeding, he was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of first-degree murder for a shooting and sentenced to death. The court found that it was not error to restrict defendant from questioning the jurors about a note they sent to the judge expressing concern that the defendant was writing down their names, finding that he had been given the opportunity to question the jurors about prospective bias they may have had about him. The court found no plain error during the capital sentencing for allowing the testimony of a witness about defendant's prior assault on her husband and the effect the attack had on her life. It was not error to refuse to submit the statutory mitigator that the murder was committed while defendant was under the influence of mental or emotional disturbance under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(f)(2) because the evidence did not support the contention.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant received a fair trial, free of prejudicial error, and that the sentence of death had to be left undisturbed.

State v. Cagle

SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


346 N.C. 497; 488 S.E.2d 535; 1997 N.C. LEXIS 475


April 14, 1997, Heard in the Supreme Court  
July 24, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied December 15, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7581.
Writ of certiorari denied Cagle v. North Carolina, 522 U.S. 1032, 118 S. Ct. 635, 139 L. Ed. 2d 614, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7581 (1997)
Motion dismissed by State v. Cagle, 547 S.E.2d 439, 2001 N.C. LEXIS 250 (N.C., 2001)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Bacon v. Lee, 353 N.C. 696, 549 S.E.2d 840, 2001 N.C. LEXIS 831 (2001)
Writ denied by State v. Cagle, 356 N.C. 168, 568 S.E.2d 616, 2002 N.C. LEXIS 738 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cagle v. Branker, 2008 U.S. App. LEXIS 5643 (4th Cir. N.C., Mar. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death as to defendant Cagle and a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment as to defendant Scott entered by Weeks, J., on 15 June 1995 in Superior Court, Cumberland County, upon jury verdicts of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendants' motions to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments imposed as to each defendant for robbery with a dangerous weapon and conspiracy to commit robbery with a dangerous weapon were allowed on 15 October 1996.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged their convictions from the Superior Court, Cumberland County (North Carolina), for robbery with a dangerous weapon and conspiracy to commit robbery with a dangerous weapon. In addition, one defendant received the death penalty both for first-degree murder on the basis of premeditation and deliberation and under the felony murder rule, and the other received life imprisonment for first-degree felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, convicted for robbery and murder, claimed error, but the court found that defendants opened the door to evidence about killing a cat at the murder scene; the evidence was probative on the issue of intent, state of mind, or for context; and it was relevant to explain or rebut evidence elicited in cross-examining the state's witnesses, when defendants implied that another man acted independently and that they were only joking about a plan. The court found that one of them communicated his premeditated plan, fled, and used an alibi, so the trial court did not err in refusing a voluntary intoxication instruction. The court found that the death penalty was not based on passion, prejudice, or arbitrariness, and the sentence was proportionate because the murder occurred in the victim's home, defendant fled while the victim was alive but did not seek medical help, and defendant used the victim's homosexuality to induce him into a vulnerable position. The court asserted that no confrontation rights were violated and that one defendant's intent was irrelevant because they acted in concert. The court held that no mistrial was warranted and that the sentences would be undisturbed.


OUTCOME: The court rejected defendants' claims of error regarding their convictions for robbery and murder, holding that they received a fair trial and sentencing, free from prejudicial error, and the sentences as entered, a death sentence and life imprisonment, would be left undisturbed. Intoxication did not negate one defendant's premeditation and deliberation. Defendants induced the victim to be vulnerable in his home where he expected to be secure.

Leandro v. State

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 and on appeal of right of a constitutional question pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) to review a unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 122 N.C. App. 1, 468 S.E.2d 543 (1996), reversing an order entered by Braswell, J., on 1 February 1995 in the Superior Court, Halifax County, denying defendants' motion to dismiss.
Leandro v. State, 122 N.C. App. 1, 468 S.E.2d 543, 1996 N.C. App. LEXIS 201 (1996)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, school boards, students, parents or guardians from poor school systems, and intervenors, school boards, students, parents or guardians from wealthy urban schools, sought review of a reversal by a state appellate court (North Carolina) of the trial court's denial of a motion to dismiss by defendants, state and its Board of Education. The suit alleged that the educational funding system violated the state's constitution.


OVERVIEW: Education boards, students, and their parents or guardians from poor school systems filed suit against the state and its Board of Education, alleging that the current funding system denied their rights under the state's constitution. Education boards, students, and their parents or guardians from wealthy urban schools intervened alleging that their educational needs were also being inadequately considered. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss, which the appellate court reversed. The court held that the state's constitution: (1) guaranteed the right to a free public education; (2) required that an education prepare students to participate and compete in the society or the education was inadequate; (3) guaranteed the opportunity to receive a sound basic education; (4) under N.C. Const. art. IX, § 2(1) did not require substantially equal funding or equal advantages; and (5) did not guarantee a right to equal educational opportunities in the various school districts of the state. The court held that sufficient allegations were made regarding the state's supplemental funding system and violations of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 115C to justify further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the appellate court's decision, which reversed the trial court's denial of the motion to dismiss by the state and its Board of Education. The court remanded the case for the appellate court for further remand to the trial court for further proceedings.
