State v. Walls


No. 42A93 - Northampton


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


342 N.C. 1; 463 S.E.2d 738; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 537


March 13, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
November 3, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Brown (Frank R.), J., at the 11 January 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Northampton County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury conviction was allowed by this Court on 6 July 1994.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court, Northampton County (North Carolina) of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed a three-year-old boy by throwing him into a river. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress his statements, that because he was intoxicated he could not formulate the specific intent to kill, and that his rights were violated when the trial court refused to admit allegedly relevant mitigating evidence during the sentencing proceeding. The court affirmed. Defendant's remarks were volunteered statements, and the detective's questions did not convert the conversation into an interrogation. The trial court found as fact that defendant was coherent and not confused, and that although defendant had been drinking, he was not under the influence of alcohol. The trial court then concluded as a matter of law that defendant voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently waived his rights. Defendant failed to carry his burden to produce substantial evidence which would support a conclusion by the judge that he was so intoxicated that he could not form a deliberate and premeditated intent to kill. The proposed testimony was not relevant and admissible under the auspices of allowing jurors to reconsider any guilt phase residual doubts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death.

State v. Alston


No. 416A92 - Warren


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


341 N.C. 198; 461 S.E.2d 687; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 406


February 14, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
September 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected. Certiorari Denied February 26, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1442.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Allen (J.B., Jr.), J., at the 19 October 1992 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Warren County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Criminal Session of Superior Court, Warren County (North Carolina) that convicted him of first-degree murder on the theory of premeditation and deliberation and that sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Testimony during defendant's trial for the first-degree murder of his girlfriend indicated that although she suffered from blunt-force injuries, she died as a result of suffocation. Defendant was convicted based on premeditation and deliberation and was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found no error, holding that the jury selection and the guilt and sentencing phases of defendant's trial were free from prejudicial error and that the death sentence was not disproportionate. In analyzing the jury selection phase, the court found that the exclusion of jurors with a bias against the death penalty that might have impeded their ability to follow the law was proper and that defendant's failure to raise a Batson objection precluded him from raising the issue on appeal. During the guilt phase, the trial court properly ruled on the admissibility of defendant's prior assault on the victim, state of mind statements by witnesses, and defendant's conduct before and after the murder, and the prosecutor did not act improperly during his closing argument. Because of the nature of the crime and the aggravating circumstances, the death sentence was not disproportionate as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court found that defendant, who was convicted of first-degree murder based on premeditation and deliberation and who was sentenced to death, received a fair trial and sentencing proceeding, free of prejudicial error.

State v. McLaughlin


No. 637A84(3) - Bladen


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


341 N.C. 426; 462 S.E.2d 1; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 405


October 11, 1994, Heard In The Supreme Court  
September 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected. Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1254.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment sentencing him to death entered by Brooks, J., at the 8 February 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Bladen County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), from a judgment of the Criminal Session of the Superior Court of Bladen County (North Carolina), which sentenced defendant to death for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to death for first-degree murders of three individuals. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to show that all of the murders were sufficiently connected to be parts of one course of conduct by defendant. The trial court did not err in admitting the evidence in question as evidence tending to establish the course of conduct aggravating circumstance, and the fact that the jury did not find this aggravating circumstance was irrelevant to the outcome of this issue. Further, the court held that the trial court's failure to give a peremptory instruction, which may have caused one or more jurors to fail to find as a mitigating circumstance that defendant worked as a cook in the prison, was harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt. The court concluded that the record fully supported the aggravating circumstances found by the jury. There was no indication that the death sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary consideration. Finally, the court held that the sentence of death entered in the case was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendant's capital sentencing proceeding was free of prejudicial error and that the resulting sentence of death was not disproportionate; thus, the sentence of death entered against defendant was left undisturbed.

 

78 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


McIntyre v. McIntyre


No. 142PA94 - Buncombe


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


341 N.C. 629; 461 S.E.2d 745; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 409


May 8, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
September 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31, prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals, of an order entered 19 October 1993 by Cash, J., in District Court, Buncombe County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents challenged the decision of the District Court, Buncombe County (North Carolina), which dismissed the grandparents complaint against defendant parents seeking visitation of their grandchildren based on the conclusion that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 50-13.1(a) (1994) was unconstitutional in that it deprived the parents of their right to determine with whom their children would associate.


OVERVIEW: The legislature's creation of special statutes to provide for grandparents' visitation rights suggested that it did not intend § 50-13.1(a) as a broad grant to grandparents of the right to visitation when the natural parents had legal custody of their children and were living with them as an intact family. The legislature intended to grant grandparents a right to visitation only in the situations specified in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 50-13.2(b1) (1987), N.C. Gen. Stat. § 50-13.5(j) (1994), and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 50-13.2A (1987). Had it intended otherwise, it would have repealed the specific statutes when it amended § 50-13.1(a), the general statute. The court found that although the 1989 amendment probably was added to provide that in certain contexts "custody" and "visitation" were synonymous, in the context of grandparents' rights to visitation, the two words were not synonymous. The court held that § 50-13.1(a) did not grant grandparents the right to seek visitation when no custody proceeding was ongoing and the minor children's family was intact. Thus, the court determined that § 50-13.1(a) did not apply. Therefore, the court did not address the constitutionality of § 50-13.1(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the grandparents' action seeking visitation of their grandchildren.

State v. Simpson


No. 43A93 - Rockingham

341 N.C. 316; 462 S.E.2d 191; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 402

September 8, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Simpson v. North Carolina, 516 U.S. 1161, 116 S. Ct. 1048, 134 L. Ed. 2d 194, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1635 (1996)
Writ denied by State v. Simpson, 627 S.E.2d 470, 2006 N.C. LEXIS 1473 (N.C., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Davis (James C.), J., at a resentencing proceeding held at the 11 January 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Rockingham County, upon defendant's conviction of first-degree murder.
State v. Simpson, 331 N.C. 267, 415 S.E.2d 351, 1992 N.C. LEXIS 204 (1992)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Rockingham County (North Carolina), which imposed a sentence of death upon him after he pleaded guilty to one count of first degree murder, one count of robbery with a dangerous weapon, and one count of conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: In challenging his death sentence, defendant claimed the trial court erred in unduly restricting questions during voir dire about whether a prospective juror could consider imposing both a death sentence and life imprisonment on a convicted murderer and whether he would consider both aggravating and mitigating circumstances. Error was alleged in the excusals for cause granted to the state for five prospective jurors, in the trial court's refusal to give a peremptory instruction on several mitigating circumstances, and in its refusal to allow an expert witness for defendant to testify about his emotional or mental disturbances. The court found that the voir dire sufficiently covered attitudes regarding the death penalty, and thus, even assuming proper questions were excluded, their exclusion was harmless. The court also found a sufficient basis to show impermissible bias with respect to the jurors excused for cause, that the peremptory instructions were not required because the evidence on the mitigating circumstances was conflicting, and that any error in the restriction of testimony of the expert witness was harmless because other witnesses sufficiently covered the subject matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that imposed a sentence of death upon defendant.

State v. Burr

SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA

September 8, 1995, Filed

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Burr v. Branker, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 38757 (M.D.N.C., May 5, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Stanback, J., at the 1 March 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Alamance County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to the additional judgment imposed for assault on a female and conviction for felony child abuse was allowed 13 July 1994.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court, Alamance County (North Carolina) of first-degree murder, assault on a female, and felony child abuse, and a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved in with the victim's mother two months before the murder. Defendant and the mother argued through the day and defendant assaulted the mother, as he had done previously. The mother left the defendant in charge of the sleeping infant. Upon her return, she noticed the infant was in distress and bruised, which defendant attributed to grease marks. Defendant refused to take the child to the hospital until the mother said she would call an ambulance, and defendant stopped for gas on the way. Medical testimony established numerous injuries, including broken arms and legs and a skull fracture, consistent with shaken baby syndrome. Defendant asserted 25 points of error. In the handful of instances in which the arguments had any merit, the court held any error was harmless. The court then conducted a mandatory proportionality review required by N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(d)(2) and found the penalty was not disproportionate or excessive. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because defendant received a fair trial and the sentencing proceeding was free from prejudicial error.

State v. McCarver


No. 384A92 - Cabarrus


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


341 N.C. 364; 462 S.E.2d 25; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 404


September 12, 1994, Heard In The Supreme Court  
September 8, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Freeman, J., at the 8 September 1992 Special Criminal Session of Superior Court, Cabarrus County. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his robbery with a dangerous weapon conviction was allowed by the Supreme Court 8 February 1994.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Cabarrus County (North Carolina), convicted the defendant of murder in the first degree and robbery with a dangerous weapon. The trial court sentenced the defendant to 40 years' imprisonment for the robbery conviction and to death for the murder conviction. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant and an accomplice robbed the victim and murdered him with a knife. On appeal, the court held that (1) the defendant did not show prejudice during voir dire because he did not exhaust his peremptory challenges, (2) the defendant's right of presence had not attached during the pretrial screening of the venire because it was not a part of the capital trial, (3) the prosecutor's comment on the previous trial was neutral and did not diminish the jurors' understanding of their responsibilities, (4) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the defendant's motion for mistrial based on prosecutorial misconduct, (5) defense counsel acted properly, (6) the trial court correctly instructed the jury regarding the doctrine of acting in concert, (7) the trial court's instruction on inferences was not plain error, (8) the trial court correctly instructed the jury that their sentencing recommendations had to be unanimous, and (9) the trial court properly instructed the jury regarding mitigating and aggravating circumstances. The court performed a proportionality review and determined that the death penalty was not disproportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of the defendant for robbery and murder and affirmed the sentences imposed.

 

82 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garner


No. 342A93-2 - Robeson


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 573; 459 S.E.2d 718; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 390


April 10, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1200.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing two sentences of death entered by Battle, J., on 3 September 1993 in the Superior Court, Robeson County.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Robeson County (North Carolina) sentenced defendant to death upon his conviction for two murders. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering two people. These murders took place during a several day crime spree. Defendant was sentenced to death on each of these murder charges, and he appealed. The court affirmed. Defendant alleged several errors on appeal. Defendant first contended that the prosecutor selected his case for capital trial in an arbitrary manner in violation of defendant's constitutional rights. Capital punishment was not rendered unconstitutional simply because the prosecutor was granted broad discretion in deciding which cases to try capitally. Therefore, in order to prevail on his claim, defendant had to show that the decision to try him capitally was motivated by a discriminatory purpose and had a discriminatory effect. Defendant did not make this showing. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence taken from his residence during a search consented to by his girlfriend. A search was not unreasonable if lawful consent to search was given. A third party could give permission to search where she possessed common authority over or other sufficient relationship to the premises or effects sought to be inspected.


OUTCOME: The judgment sentencing defendant to death upon his two convictions for murder was affirmed.

 

83 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lyons


No. 379A94 - Forsyth


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 646; 459 S.E.2d 770; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 391


April 13, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment entered by Rousseau, J., at the 1 November 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Forsyth County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and life sentence imposed by the Superior Court, Forsyth County (North Carolina) on charges of first degree murder because the trial court denied his motion to dismiss, improperly instructed the jury on specific intent and transferred intent, refused to instruct the jury on self-defense, habitation, voluntary and involuntary manslaughter, and because the prosecutor purportedly withheld Brady evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried capitally for the first degree murder of a police officer. A jury convicted defendant, but was deadlocked as to the death penalty. Pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(b), the court imposed a sentence of life imprisonment. Defendant challenged the conviction and sentence. The court found no error. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to support a conviction on first degree murder charges. The court also held that there was no error in the trial court's specific intent to kill instructions. Further, the found that appellant was not entitled to the defense of habitation or of perfect self-defense because there was no reasonable belief that it was necessary to shoot the officer. Further, the court held that defendant suffered no prejudice by the exclusion of the lesser-included charges of voluntary and involuntary manslaughter. The court held that defendant's transfer of intent argument was waived and was beyond the court's scope of review, that the jury questionnaire was proper, that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in the admission and exclusion of evidence, and that the prosecution did not withhold exculpatory Brady evidence.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court committed no error in convicting and sentencing defendant on first degree murder charges because there was evidence supporting the conviction, the specific intent charge, and the transferred intent challenge was waived, defendant was not entitled to an instruction on self-defense and habitation, was not entitled to be charged with lesser-included offenses, and the prosecutor did not withhold Brady evidence.

State v. Lynch


No. 242A93 - Gaston


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 435; 459 S.E.2d 679; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 361


February 13, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing two sentences of death entered by Sitton, J., at the 26 April 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Gaston County, upon two jury verdicts of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments imposed for two counts of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury, one count of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill, five counts of assault with a deadly weapon on a law enforcement officer, six counts of assault by discharging a firearm into occupied property, and seven counts of injury to personal property was allowed 6 July 1994.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right, pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), from judgments in the Superior Court of Gaston County (North Carolina), which imposed two sentences of death upon convictions for first-degree murder and multiple assaultive and weapons crimes. He claimed error in the jury selection, the guilt-innocence phase, the sentencing, and in the proportionality of his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that he should have been able to question jurors on mitigating factors during voir dire, the sentencing was prejudicial, and the death sentences were disproportionate. The court disagreed with all of defendant's contentions. The court held that no abuse of discretion occurred and that defendant was not allowed to examine jurors on how they would deliberate during voir dire. The court also held that where no offer of proof was made after objections were sustained, they were not preserved for appellate review. Moreover, no error occurred when the jury was instructed to consider defendant's sanity only after it had considered defendant's mental ability to formulate the specific intent to kill as these are two different concepts, and no improper shifting of the burden of proof occurred at trial. Finally, the sentencing proceeding was not improper because evidence viewed in the light most favorable to the State supported submission of the especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel circumstance instruction based on the particular aggravating circumstance or circumstances found by the jury during the sentencing proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court found no error, and it affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court Pitt County (North Carolina), which imposed the death penalty upon a jury verdict of guilty of two counts of first degree murder, two counts of first-degree kidnapping and rape, and one count of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried capitally on indictments charging him with first-degree murders of women. The jury returned verdicts finding defendant guilty of each count of first-degree murder on the theories of both premeditation and deliberation and felony murder. State v. Daughtry


No. 412A93 - Johnston


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 488; 459 S.E.2d 747; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 377


April 11, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed

Writ denied by, in part, Stay granted by State v. Daughtry, 343 N.C. 754, 477 S.E.2d 34, 1996 N.C. LEXIS 669 (1996)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Daughtry v. Polk, 190 Fed. Appx. 262, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 17962 (4th Cir. N.C., 2006)
Motion granted by State v. Daughtry, 2010 N.C. LEXIS 574 (N.C., Aug. 16, 2010)
Motion granted by State v. Daughtry, 2010 N.C. LEXIS 717 (N.C., Sept. 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Barnette, J., at the 20 September 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Johnston County, on a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Superior Court of Johnston County (North Carolina), a jury convicted defendant of first degree murder and first-degree sexual offense and sentenced him to death. The jury found two aggravating circumstances: the crime was especially heinous and was committed while engaged in a sex offense; one statutory mitigating circumstance, that defendant suffered a mental or emotional disturbance; and 14 nonstatutory mitigating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant had received a fair trial and that the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate. Defendant had committed a brutal, merciless, and dehumanizing attack, which included severe blunt-trauma injuries and a depraved sexual offense. The record contained overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, including his confession, DNA results, and blood-type matching. The evidence supported the aggravating circumstances under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(e)(9), (e)(5), (f)(1), and (f)(7). The victim had numerous injuries to her head, face, neck, chest, back, hands, and arms, as well as her rectum and vagina. Defendant's prior criminal history included his numerous beatings of the victim, an incident in which he shot a man, and a conviction for assault. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by finding that he voluntarily reinitiated interrogation after requesting a lawyer by saying, "let's go ahead and talk." The court disagreed and found that he was not in custody at the time because he knew he was free to leave, and he was never handcuffed, frisked, or threatened.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

State v. Knight


No. 110A94 - Forsyth


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA

July 28, 1995, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment entered by Mills, J., at the 3 May 1993 Mixed Session of Superior Court, Forsyth County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Mixed Session of Superior Court, Forsyth County (North Carolina), which entered a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment following a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, that the challenged evidence was inadmissible because it was obtained as the result of an illegal search after entry into his house, and that the trial court erroneously denied his motion to suppress his statement to the police. The court held that exigent circumstances existed justifying the forced entry of the police officers into defendant's residence after notification and a brief delay. The court concluded that there was competent evidence to support the trial court's findings of fact that the search warrant was on the premises when the police entered defendant's residence and that it was read before any search was undertaken in the house. The court also held that the trial court held a voir dire to determine the admissibility of defendant's statement, and its findings of fact after such a hearing were conclusive and binding on the court because they were supported by competent evidence even though the evidence was conflicting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Littlejohn


No. 125A93 - Mecklenburg


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 750; 459 S.E.2d 629; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 385


October 10, 1994, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing sentences of life imprisonment entered by Lamm, J., at the 21 September 1992 Mixed Session of Superior Court, Mecklenburg County, upon jury verdicts of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendants' motions to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional sentences imposed were allowed 21 December 1993.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from judgments entered by the Superior Court, Mecklenburg County (North Carolina), which found them guilty of first-degree murder and imposed sentences of life imprisonment following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' cases were consolidated for trial, at which the state's evidence established that defendants were parties to the fatal stabbing of the victim. On appeal, defendant one asserted that the admission of defendant two's confession violated his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation because the confession implicated him. The court held that assuming the introduction of the confession was error, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the evidence against defendant one was strong and corroborated. Moreover, defendant one was guilty of felony murder by his own statement, and therefore, his conviction was affirmed. The court also affirmed defendant two's conviction and rejected his numerous assignments of error. Defendant two's confession was not obtained in violation of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-501(2) simply because he was interrogated by police before he was taken before a magistrate. The police fully advised defendant two of his constitutional rights. Moreover, the fact that defendant two's confession was admitted in a redacted form did not violate his rights because he was not prejudiced by it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions and sentences.

State v. Powell


No. 190A93 - Cleveland


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 674; 459 S.E.2d 219; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 388


February 15, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Gaines, J., at the 12 April 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Cleveland County, on a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Cleveland County (North Carolina), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the victim, who was working at a store, was brutally murdered by blows to her head with a tire iron. An eyewitness identified defendant as being outside the store shortly before the murder. At a police interview, defendant admitted to "going off on" the victim and then requested that his Miranda waiver be ripped up so that he could talk off the record after which he recounted the details of the crime. Defendant asserted numerous errors. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court concluded that defendant's confession was not involuntarily induced by the ripping up the Miranda waiver. The court found that defendant had already voluntarily confessed and had been identified by the eyewitness. In addition, the court determined that a taped conversation between defendant and a friend was also admissible because it was not taped at the request of the police. The court found that the sentence was not disproportionate to the crime considering its brutality and the absence of any mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court concluded that defendant had received a fair trial, free of prejudicial error, and that defendant's death sentence was not disproportionate to the circumstances of his conviction of first-degree murder.

Leete v. County of Warren


No. 308A94 - Warren


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


341 N.C. 116; 462 S.E.2d 476; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 778


March 15, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
July 28, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by plaintiffs pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(1) from the unanimous decision of the Court of Appeals, 114 N.C. App. 755, 443 S.E.2d 98 (1994), reversing an order entered by Ellis (B. Craig), J., on 25 March 1993 in Superior Court, Warren County.

Previously Reported at: 459 S.E.2d 232 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which reversed a trial court order permanently enjoining defendant county board of commissioners (board) from giving severance pay to the county manager.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed suit alleging that the board unlawfully authorized severance pay to the county manager upon his voluntary resignation. The trial court granted an order permanently enjoining the board from making the payment. The court of appeals reversed the order, and on further appeal, the court reversed that decision and reinstated the trial court order. The court held that there was a presumption that public officials discharged their duties in good faith and exercised their powers according to the law. The presumption placed a heavy burden on any party challenging the validity of public officials' actions to overcome the presumption by competent and substantial evidence. The court found that the taxpayers met their burden. N.C. Const. art. I, § 32 precluded exclusive or separate emoluments except in consideration of public services. All compensation due the county manager under the terms of his employment had been paid. Any additional compensation would be compensation beyond that due for services rendered and, thus, constitutionally impermissible. There was no written contract providing for severance pay or additional compensation beyond a salary for services rendered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and reinstated the trial court's order enjoining the board from giving severance pay to the county manager.

State v. White


No. 487A93 - Martin


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 264; 457 S.E.2d 841; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 260


January 12, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
June 2, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment entered by Griffin, J., at the 12 April 1993 Special Criminal Session of Superior Court, Martin County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from a judgement of the Superior Court, Martin County (North Carolina), which convicted her of first-degree murder, and sentenced her to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried noncapitally for the first-degree murder of her stepson. Defendant put on no evidence at trial. Defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court abused its discretion by denying her motion to continue the trial until after her capital trial for the murder of her husband. The court held that defendant's alleged "Hobson's choice" between asserting her privilege against self-incrimination and her right to testify on her own behalf was illusory. The trial court's denial of her motion for a continuance did not force defendant to choose between these two constitutional rights but to make a purely tactical decision as to whether it would be more advantageous to testify in that trial, in her capital trial, in both trials, or not at all. Defendant also argued that the trial court committed reversible error by admitting irrelevant evidence concerning the life insurance policy on her stepson, in violation of her right to a fair trial. The court held that the evidence that defendant became one of the beneficiaries of an insurance policy on her stepson's life days before he was killed was relevant to show her motive for murdering her stepson.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgement below.

State v. Taylor


No. 483A93 - Craven


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


340 N.C. 52; 455 S.E.2d 859; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 167


January 11, 1995, Heard In The Supreme Court  
April 7, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment entered by Phillips, J., at the 20 November 1991 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Craven County, upon a jury verdict of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to an additional judgment imposed for robbery with a dangerous weapon was allowed 1 December 1993.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling from the Superior Court, Craven County (North Carolina), which sentenced defendant to life imprisonment on conviction for first degree murder and a consecutive 40-year term for robbery with a dangerous weapon. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to the additional term for robbery was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was linked to the victim's stabbing death by a blood-stained shirt and a latent fingerprint on a bloody piece of wood. Witnesses identified the shirt as one that defendant wore the night of the murder; the witnesses saw defendant again later that night wearing a different shirt. Defendant told the witnesses that he had killed a woman. Defendant was convicted and sentenced. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that there was no reasonable likelihood that the jury would have understood the term "moral certainty," which the trial court had included in a jury instruction at defendant's request, to be dissociated from the evidence. The language clearly directed the jury to base its decision on the evidence. The prosecutor's questions on closing argument: Where is his alibi? Where was he? did not merit a mistrial. The remarks were directed solely to defendant's failure to offer evidence to rebut the state's case and were in response to defendant's jury argument; they were not an impermissible comment on defendant's failure to testify. A tardy production of Brady material did not merit a mistrial; defendant failed to show prejudice thereby.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and robbery with a dangerous weapon and consecutive sentences of life and 40 years. The court held that the trial court committed no reversible errors.

State v. Lovin


No. 192A92 - Buncombe


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 695; 454 S.E.2d 229; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 101


January 31, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
March 3, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment entered by Hyatt, J., at the 11 November 1991 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Buncombe County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder in a case in which the defendant was tried capitally. The defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments was allowed.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Criminal Session of Superior Court, Buncombe County (North Carolina), which imposed a life imprisonment sentence upon him after a jury found him guilty of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his motion to suppress evidence was improperly denied. Specifically, defendant argued that several pieces of evidence that were seized from his person was obtained as a result of an unconstitutional detention because police officers at an airport held him without any reasonable, articulable suspicion that he had been involved in a homicide. Defendant further contended that an incriminating statement made to a police officer should have been excluded because the statement was the result of an unconstitutional arrest. The court held that both the evidence and the incriminating statement were properly obtained. The court held that the police officers had sufficient justification to conduct an investigatory stop of defendant at the airport because the police had found the victim's car in the parking lot with its hood still warm, defendant fit the profile of the suspect in the case, and a clerk directed them to defendant who had purchased a ticket with the victim's credit card. The court held that defendant's incriminating statements were proper because the arrest was not illegal since the police had sufficient justification to arrest defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court because the police had sufficient justification to conduct an investigatory stop of defendant.

 

95 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Conaway


No. 389A92 - Richmond


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 487; 453 S.E.2d 824; 1995 N.C. LEXIS 26


September 13, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
February 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Helms, J., at the 5 October 1992 Special Criminal Session of Superior Court, Richmond County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of two counts of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments imposed for two counts of first-degree kidnapping, one count of robbery with a dangerous weapon, and one count of misdemeanor larceny was granted 20 December 1992.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right the sentence of death imposed by the Special Criminal Session of Superior Court, Richmond County (North Carolina), upon a jury verdict which found him guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant moved to bypass the appeals court as to the additional judgments imposed for first-degree kidnapping, robbery with a dangerous weapon, and misdemeanor larceny was granted.


OVERVIEW: While on parole, defendant robbed, kidnapped, carjacked, and murdered two people. Three witnesses implicated defendant, who was later arrested. The court held that the jury selection, guilt-innocence phase, and sentencing proceeding of defendant's trial were free from prejudicial error and the death sentence was not disproportionate to the crime. The court found that: (1) defendant did not object to various issues, thereby failing to preserve them on appeal; (2) denial of his motion to prevent the exercise of peremptory challenges to the jurors who disfavored the death penalty was proper; (3) there was no prejudice from the denial to sequester the three codefendants; (4) the jury found that the mitigating circumstances outweighed the aggravating circumstances; (5) defendant delayed bringing critical information to the trial court's attention; (6) defendant made evidence of his prior convictions an issue; (7) the prosecutor's statements were not prejudicial; (8) photographs of the victim's bodies were relevant; and (9) defendant's death sentence was not imposed under the influence of prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the imposition of the death sentence.

State v. Baker


No. 159A92 - Wilson


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


338 N.C. 526; 451 S.E.2d 574; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 727


November 15, 1993, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Butterfield, J., at the 30 March 1992 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Wilson County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. On 30 April 1992 this Court granted a stay of execution pending defendant's appeal. On 7 May 1992 this Court also granted defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments imposed for first-degree kidnapping and common-law robbery.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his jury trial, defendant appealed his convictions and sentences by the Superior Court, Wilson County (North Carolina) for first-degree kidnapping, robbery with a dangerous weapon, and first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the murder of his estranged wife, first-degree kidnapping, and robbery with a dangerous weapon. He was tried capitally for the murder and found guilty on the theory of premeditation and deliberations. In accordance with the jury's unanimous recommendation following a capital sentencing proceeding, defendant was sentenced to death. He was also convicted of and sentenced on the other charges. On appeal, the court held that the jury selection and guilt-innocence phases of defendant's trial were free from prejudicial error, but remanded for a new capital sentencing proceeding because of error. As to the capital sentencing proceeding, the court held that the trial court erred in instructing the jury as to statutory mitigating circumstances. The trial court erred in submitting mitigating circumstances because in its instruction it varied the wording of a statutory mitigating circumstance, and the instruction permitted the jurors to decide such circumstance was without weight. The court held that it could not conclude that such an error was harmless beyond a doubt and, therefore, defendant was entitled to a new capital sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decisions regarding jury selection and the guilt-innocence phases of defendant's trial. The court held that the trial court erred in the capital sentencing procedure and remanded for a new proceeding.

 

97 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spruill


No. 404A92 - Northampton


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


338 N.C. 612; 452 S.E.2d 279; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 732


March 17, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Britt (Joe Freeman), J., at the 12 October 1992 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Northampton County, upon a plea of guilty to first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Northampton County (North Carolina), which convicted defendant for first-degree murder, based upon a guilty plea, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the murder of his girlfriend and was sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant argued that the state exercised its peremptory challenges in a racially discriminatory manner. Defendant also argued that the trial court failed to instruct the jury that if it granted defendant life imprisonment, it would be life without the possibility of parole. The court held that where most of the witnesses, defendant, and the victim were black, a jury composed of six whites and six blacks did not violate Batson. The court held that parole and parole eligibility were not proper matters for jury consideration in a capital sentencing. The court held that the prosecution's inadvertent reference to death row did not constitute a transgression so highly prejudicial that it alone constituted the source of adverse impression, if any, in the minds of the jurors. The court held that the prosecutor's improper statements during closing did not prejudice defendant. The court held that defendant received a fair trial and capital sentencing proceeding free of prejudicial error and that the death penalty was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder and the sentence of death.

State v. Carter


No. 160A92 - Wayne


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


338 N.C. 569; 451 S.E.2d 157; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 715


January 31, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Griffin, J., at the 10 April 1992 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Wayne County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to an additional judgment imposed for attempted second-degree rape was allowed by this Court on 14 July 1993.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed as of right under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a) from the Criminal Session of Superior Court, Wayne County (North Carolina), a judgment upon the jury's verdict that found him guilty of first-degree murder and attempted second-degree rape. Defendant also appealed the death sentence imposed under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to proceed pro se. Defendant was allowed to waive in-court representation by counsel, once the statutory inquiry under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1242 occurred because the trial judge's colloquy with defendant established that he clearly and unequivocally waived his right to counsel, and that waiver was knowing, intelligent, and voluntary. The prosecutor's proffered explanations for preemptory challenges of prospective black jurors under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1212(9) (1993), satisfied the Batson test and were not race-based when the reasons for the challenges included the jurors' lack of candor, and family that had engaged in prior felonious criminal activity. During sentencing it was not error to admit a prior crime of assault in rebuttal to defendant's evidence that he was generally of good character and as to the mitigating factors of his age, that he was a loving father of two children, and had adapted well to prison. After a proportionality review pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15-2000(d)(2), it was determined that the sentence was not excessive or disproportionate to that imposed in similar affirmed cases considering the crime and defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions based upon its conclusion that there were no procedural errors committed during the trial and sentencing proceedings. The death sentence was also confirmed after the court determined that the sentence was not disproportionate to the nature of the crimes.

State v. Hunt


No. 17A91 - Forsyth


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 622; 457 S.E.2d 276; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 717


February 17, 1993, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Issuance of the Mandate in this case is temporarily stayed pending further orders of the Court. January 19, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of life imprisonment entered by Ferrell, J., at the 17 September 1990 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Catawba County, upon a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of first-degree murder.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Catawba County (North Carolina) that imposed a sentence of life imprisonment upon defendant pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-17 (1992) after finding him guilty of first degree murder; defendant alleged errors involving evidence, testimony, trial conduct, and prosecutorial conduct.


OVERVIEW: After his initial conviction for first degree murder was overturned, defendant was retried noncapitally, convicted of first degree felony murder, and given a mandatory life sentence pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 14-17 (1992). Defendant appealed. The court found that (1) the admission of defendant's testimony at the first trial had been proper and any earlier objection to such testimony had been waived by the failure to object at the second trial, (2) the prosecutor's conduct, including closing arguments, had not risen to a level sufficient to constitute reversible error, (3) the failure to intervene ex mero motu to stop improper prosecutorial conduct had not been a violation of defendant's constitutional rights, (4) the jury charges, including the charge on reasonable doubt, had been proper, (5) the admission of an accomplice's testimony from the first trial had also been proper, (6) there had been no error in admitting an in-court identification of defendant where that identification had originated independently of any illegal lineup, (7) other decisions regarding evidence and testimony at trial had been proper, and (8) therefore the judgment and sentence were proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

 

100 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rose


No. 32A92 - Rockingham


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 172; 451 S.E.2d 211; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 718


April 14, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from judgments imposing two sentences of death entered by Wood, J., at the 2 December 1991 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Rockingham County. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to additional judgments imposing sentences of imprisonment entered upon his conviction for two counts of robbery with a dangerous weapon was allowed 23 August 1993.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Rockingham County (North Carolina), which imposed two death sentences on defendant on the recommendation of the jury after he was convicted of two counts of first degree murder. He was also sentenced to a prison term as to his convictions for armed robbery of the victims, which were the subject of a separate appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder and the trial court imposed two death sentences. Defendant appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and death sentences. The trial court did not commit error by denying defendant's motion for change of venue because defendant failed to meet his burden of proving that pretrial publicity tainted his chances of receiving a fair and impartial trial. The evidence of defendant's prior prison escape and thefts was properly admitted to establish defendant's intent and motive for the murders at issue, and the evidence was more probative than prejudicial. Defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on second degree murder because the state's evidence was positive as to each element of first degree murder and there was no conflicting evidence relating to any of the elements. The prosecutor did not deny defendant a fair trial by arguing that the jury should apply an unconstitutional definition of the reasonable doubt standard because the prosecutor's definition did not lower the state's burden of proof. Due to three aggravating factors being found, the death sentence was not disproportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions on two counts of first degree murder because the trial court's rulings were proper and sufficient evidence supported the jury's decision. The court affirmed defendant's two death sentences because they did not violate the Eighth or Fourteenth Amendments and they were not disproportionate to the crimes.

State v. Williams


No. 264A90-2 - Wayne


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 1; 452 S.E.2d 245; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 720



December 30, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. As Corrected June 20, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: On remand by the Supreme Court of the United States,     U.S.    , 128 L. Ed. 2d 42 (1994), for further consideration in light of Victor v. Nebraska, 511 U.S.    , 127 L. Ed. 2d 583, 114 S. Ct. 1239 (1994).
North Carolina v. Bryant, 511 U.S. 1001, 114 S. Ct. 1365, 128 L. Ed. 2d 42, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 2493 (1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder and other offenses and his sentence of capital punishment. After remand by the United States Supreme Court in light of a recent opinion, it was concluded by the court that a reasonable doubt instruction that had been given during defendant's trial was free from error. The case was before the court for consideration of defendant's remaining points of error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for first-degree murder and his capital sentence. The court upheld the conviction and the sentence. The court held that the trial court's ruling that the prosecutor had not exercised his peremptory challenges in a racially discriminatory could not be clearly erroneous because the trial judge chose one of two permissible views of the evidence. The court held that while ex parte conferences between the trial judge and prospective jurors did violate defendant's right to be present at all stages of the trial, the resulting error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the evidence established that his presence would have made no difference in the outcome of the conversations. The court held that the trial court did not err when it submitted defendant's borderline retardation as a nonstatutory mitigating circumstance because the evidence did not mandate submission of the statutory circumstances of impaired capacity. The court held that defendant's sentence was proportionate because the court's review of other cases in the proportionality pool did not reveal that jurors had consistently returned life sentences in cases like defendant's.


OUTCOME: Finding no prejudicial error during the trial and no disproportionality in sentencing, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and his sentence of capital punishment.

 

103 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Bowers v. City of High Point


316PA93 - Guilford


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 413; 451 S.E.2d 284; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 723


March 16, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of the decision of the Court of Appeals, 110 N.C. App. 862, 431 S.E.2d 219 (1993), affirming summary judgment entered by Ross (Thomas W.), J., in the Superior Court, Guilford County, on 20 May 1992.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiff police officers, who alleged that the city breached its contractual obligation to pay certain compensation promised in return for early retirement and also brought action for an unconstitutional impairment of contract, an unconstitutional taking, and a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The police officers had taken early retirement in reliance on the city manager's erroneous interpretation of new legislation, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 143-166.42. After the city informed the police officers that their compensation was to be reduced, they brought suit. The court reversed the appellate court decision. The court held that N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 143-166.41, 143-166.42 did not authorize the city to make separation allowances based on overtime pay, longevity pay, and accrued vacation, and that the police officers could not invoke the doctrine of estoppel to prevent the city from asserting the defense of ultra vires. The police officers' contract and constitutional actions failed because they never had a contractual right to receive payments in excess of those provided for in § 143-166.41. The Manager's representations were ultra vires, or beyond the power of the city, such that they were unenforceable. Also, the city was not estopped from asserting the ultra vires defense because the Legislature never authorized the city to enter into such separation allowance contracts, such that there was an entire absence of power, where the city only had that power that the Legislature granted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court.

State v. Pendleton


No. 478A93 - Harnett


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 379; 451 S.E.2d 274; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 729; 63 U.S.L.W. 2426


September 13, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30 of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 112 N.C. App. 171, 435 S.E.2d 100 (1993), reversing an order entered by Allen (W. Steven, Sr.), J., on 29 April 1992 in Superior Court, Harnett County.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged as of right a decision of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which reversed a superior court's dismissal of charges against him and ruled that former Chapter 74A of the General Statutes of North Carolina was a constitutional exercise of legislative power.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a religious university's campus police and arrested for driving while impaired. Defendant was convicted of driving while impaired. He appealed to the superior court for trial de novo and sought dismissal of the charge against him on the ground that former Chapter 74A of the General Statutes of North Carolina was unconstitutional. He argued that the statute authorized a religious institution to exercise the police power of the state because it permitted employees of a religious institution to be commissioned and function as police officers. The superior court dismissed the charges against him and ruled that former Chapter 74A was an unconstitutional entanglement of state and church. The court of appeals reversed and held the statute was constitutional on its face and as applied. On appeal, the court reversed and reinstated the dismissal of the charges. As applied, former Chapter 74A violated the Establishment Clause of the First Amendment. The state's delegation of its police power to the religious university was an unconstitutional delegation of an important discretionary power to a religious institution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals, reinstated the order of the superior court, and granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charges against him. The court held that the statute that permitted the religious university's employees to be police officers was unconstitutional.

Related proceeding at State v. Jones, 346 N.C. 286, 487 S.E.2d 562, 1997 N.C. LEXIS 460 (1997)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Jones v. Polk, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 4213 (4th Cir. N.C., Mar. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Strickland, J., at the 30 July 1990 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Jones County, upon a verdict of guilty of first degree murder. The defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to his convictions of assault with a deadly weapon with intent to kill inflicting serious injury and discharging a firearm into occupied property was allowed by this Court on 19 October 1992.
State v. Jones, 434 S.E.2d 217, 1993 N.C. LEXIS 663 (N.C., 1993)



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.

Am Jur 2d, Criminal Law § 628 

Validity of death penalty, under Federal Constitution, as affected by consideration of aggravating or mitigating circumstances -- Supreme Court cases. 111 L. Ed. 2d 947. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Jones County (North Carolina), which imposed a death sentence upon a verdict of guilty of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed his son and was found guilty of first degree murder. A sentence of death was imposed upon defendant. The court affirmed because defendant received a trial and sentencing proceeding that was free from prejudicial error. The death sentence was proportionate and was not by the jury out of prejudice or passion. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion during the jury selection process, which included granting the State's challenge for cause of a jury who answered that she would not be in favor of the death penalty under any circumstance. Defendant's statements to a doctor were inadmissible because they were not statements made for the purpose of medical diagnosis or treatment. It was harmless error for the trial court to fail to instruct the jury on involuntary manslaughter, because the jury was properly instructed on first and second degree murder and found defendant guilty of first degree murder based on premeditation and deliberation. There was no prejudicial error in the State's closing argument to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder and imposing a death sentence upon defendant.

State v. Basden


No. 159A93 - Duplin


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 288; 451 S.E.2d 238; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 725


October 10, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Stevens, J., at the 15 March 1993 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Duplin County, upon a jury verdict of guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals as to an additional judgment imposed for conspiracy to commit murder was granted 7 April 1994.



DISPOSITION: NO ERROR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court, Duplin County (North Carolina), which imposed a sentence of death against defendant after a jury found him guilty of first-degree murder. Defendant contended that the death sentence against him was disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder on a theory of premeditation and deliberation and recommended a sentence of death. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court held that defendant received a fair trial and sentencing proceeding and that the death penalty was not disproportionate. The court concluded that the evidence supported the jury's finding of the sole aggravating circumstance, that the murder was committed for pecuniary gain, and that the sentence of death was not imposed under the influence of any arbitrary factor. The court found that the proportionality pool included two cases that recognized the death penalty as a proportionate punishment for contract killings committed under remarkably similar circumstances. The court concluded that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because he consented to his attorney's decision to concede guilt to second-degree murder or voluntary manslaughter. The court determined that defendant could not claim that he was prejudiced by an instruction on consideration of the statutory mitigating circumstance in N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-2000(f)(6) (1988) because he invited the error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against defendant because he received a fair trial and sentencing proceeding. The death penalty was not disproportionate because the proportionality pool included two cases that recognized the death penalty as a proportionate punishment for contract killings committed under remarkably similar circumstances.

 

107 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Simeon v. Hardin


No. 267PA93 - Durham


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


339 N.C. 358; 451 S.E.2d 858; 1994 N.C. LEXIS 721


October 10, 1994, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 30, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 prior to determination by the Court of Appeals of an order granting defendant's motion to dismiss entered by Farmer, J., on 15 March 1993 in Superior Court, Durham County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff criminal defendants filed an action on behalf of themselves and of those similarly situated against defendant district attorney to challenge the district attorney's statutory authority to set the superior court's criminal trial calendar. The district attorney's motion to dismiss the action was granted by the Superior Court, Durham County (North Carolina). The criminal defendants challenged the dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The criminal defendants claimed that the district attorney used his powers to set the criminal dockets under N.C. Gen. Stat. §§ 7A-49.3 (1989), 7A-61 (1989), 15A-931 (1988) (statutes) to coerce guilty pleas. The court reversed and remanded the dismissal. The superior court had jurisdiction to hear the civil claims under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-240 (1989). The criminal defendants had standing to represent a class of those similarly situated because their claims were repetitious, yet evading review, and one case was not concluded. The statutes were constitutional under the separation of powers doctrine because the district attorney was a quasi-judicial officer and there was no intrusion on the superior court's inherent authority to manage the criminal docket. Although the statutes were constitutional under the Due Process Clause of the federal constitution and the law of the land clause under N.C. Const. art. I, § 19 because they did not facially violate the criminal defendants' rights, the criminal defendants raised a question of fact as to whether the statutes' application violated their constitutional rights. The cause was also remanded to determine class certification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of the criminal defendants' action against the district attorney to challenge the district attorney's statutory authority to set the superior court's criminal trial calendar.
