State v. Payne


No. 254A88 - Davidson


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


328 N.C. 377; 402 S.E.2d 582; 1991 N.C. LEXIS 263


December 13, 1989, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 3, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27, from a judgment imposing a sentence of death entered by Long, J., at the 10 February 1988 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Davidson County. Defendant also gave notice of appeal from his conviction and sentence of life imprisonment for rape but failed to move to bypass the Court of Appeals; this Court, sua sponte, allowed the bypass.



DISPOSITION: Case No. 83CRS16747 -- no error. Case No. 83CRS16387 -- new sentencing proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first degree rape and first degree murder, and the jury found him guilty. The Superior Court, Davidson County (North Carolina) sentenced him to life imprisonment for the first degree rape conviction and sentenced him to death for the first degree murder conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the home of an elderly woman, raped her, and killed her. There was evidence at trial that defendant's mental faculties might have been damaged by his sniffing gasoline, and that he was intoxicated at the time of the offense. Defendant claimed that his conviction should be reversed because the circumstantial evidence against him did not compel the conclusion that he was guilty. He also claimed that his death sentence should be vacated because of an improper jury instruction. The court upheld defendant's convictions, but held that he was entitled to a new sentencing proceeding on the first degree murder conviction. In so holding, the court ruled that (1) the circumstantial evidence complained of was relevant and admissible, and the weight to be given it was for the jury to decide; and (2) the trial judge erred in instructing the jury to find unanimously each mitigating circumstance before considering that circumstance in the ultimate sentencing decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first degree rape and first degree murder, but vacated the sentence imposing the death penalty and remanded the case for a new sentencing proceeding.

State v. Whittle Communications


No. 164PA90 - Wake


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


328 N.C. 456; 402 S.E.2d 556; 1991 N.C. LEXIS 265


October 10, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals of an order dismissing plaintiffs' complaint entered on 8 March 1990 by Stephens, J., at the 26 February 1990 Session of Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Wake County (North Carolina) dismissed the complaint filed by appellants, state, state board of education, and state superintendent of public instruction (State), deciding on its own motion that the complaint lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The court also declared that the contracts of appellees, company and local school boards, were not invalid under North Carolina law. The State sought discretionary review.


OVERVIEW: A private company developed educational program for viewing in public schools. Thereafter, the company entered a contract with local school boards to have the program aired in those school systems. The State then adopted a temporary rule prohibiting local school boards from entering contracts that limited the State's authority to determine the materials to be presented to students. Subsequently, the State sought to have the contracts declared void. The superior court dismissed the State's complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and ruled that the contracts were not invalid, unlawful, or unenforceable. The State sought discretionary review. On review, the court held that (1) the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over the State's complaint; (2) the State did not have the authority to enact the temporary rule concerning the contracts, because the contracts involve the selection and procurement of supplementary materials, which was an area that the general assembly had specifically placed under the control and supervision of the local school boards; and (3) the contracts did not violate the state constitution or the state's public policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

Wayne County Citizens Ass'n for Better Tax Control v. Wayne County Bd. of Comm'rs


No. 252PA90 - Wayne


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


328 N.C. 24; 399 S.E.2d 311; 1991 N.C. LEXIS 15


November 14, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
January 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review prior to determination by the Court of Appeals pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 and Rule 15 of the North Carolina Rules of Appellate Procedure, upon the joint petition of the parties, of orders of Butterfield, J., signed on 4 April 1990 and 6 April 1990, respectively, at the 26 March 1990 regular term of Superior Court, Wayne County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayer association and taxpayers, appealed a grant of summary judgment by the Superior Court, Wayne County (North Carolina) in favor of defendants, board of commissioners and commissioners, claiming that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-20 was unconstitutional and that defendants did not comply with the provisions of the statute in entering into a contract granting a security interest in real property that was subject to improvement.


OVERVIEW: Defendants entered into an installment purchase contract and granted the lender a security interest in the property. Plaintiffs brought an action challenging defendants' compliance with N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-20 and alleging that the statute was unconstitutional. They claimed that it was possible for defendants to be forced to appropriate money in the future to make contractual payments. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendants and dismissed the action. The court, after allowing the parties' joint petition to bypass the appellate court, held that the statute was constitutional. The court found that the statute barred the pledging of the taxing power to secure moneys due under a contract covered by the statute. It also clearly authorized the method of financing used by defendants, which by implication included the payment of the debt incurred. The court rejected the argument that the statute unconstitutionally allowed defendants to enter into an agreement under which they expended tax revenues in future years without a vote of the people. The court concluded that in an installment purchase contract, only the property was pledged, not the taxing power of the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for defendants.

HCA Crossroads Residential Ctrs. v. North Carolina Dep't of Human Resources, etc.


No. 79PA90 - Department of Human Resources


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


327 N.C. 573; 398 S.E.2d 466; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 989


September 4, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 (prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals) of the 21 November 1988 final decision of the Department of Human Resources denying the petitioner-appellants' applications for certificates of need for construction of chemical dependency treatment facilities.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants sought review of decisions of appellee, the North Carolina Department of Human Resources, which denied their applications for certificates of need to build adolescent chemical dependency treatment facilities.


OVERVIEW: The applicants filed applications for certificates of need to construct similar treatment facilities. For both applications, the Department allowed the maximum 150-day period under N.C. Gen. Stat. § 131E-185 (1988) to expire without action. The Department later notified the applicants that their applications were denied. The Department subsequently rejected an administrative law judge's recommendation that certificates of need be issued to both applicants. The court granted discretionary review of the Department's decisions pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-31. The court found in favor of the applicants and held that when the prescribed maximum 150-day period for review expired, the Department was deemed to have approved the applications. The court reasoned that the Department had to approve or reject the applications within the time provided by law. Once the time period expired without Department action, the Department lost subject matter jurisdiction for all purposes except to issue the certificates of need.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the Department's decisions and remanded the case to the Department.

McNeill v. Harnett County


No. 100PA90 - Harnett


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


327 N.C. 552; 398 S.E.2d 475; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 994


September 6, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
December 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30 and on discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of the decision of the Court of Appeals, 97 N.C. App. 41, 387 S.E.2d 206 (1990), affirming in part and reversing in part a judgment entered by Bowen, J., at the 25 July 1988 Civil Session of Superior Court, Harnett County, and awarding attorneys' fees for plaintiffs' attorneys.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county and sewer district, appealed from an order of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina) which held that the county's ordinance requiring the plaintiff property owners connection to sewer system to be void, instructed the county to reimburse the property owners for fees paid, and dissolved monetary judgments entered. The court of appeals also affirmed a trial court's holding which relieved the property owners of connection charges.


OVERVIEW: Property owners refused to connect their properties to a sewer system and brought a cause of action for a declaratory judgment and injunction. The county and sewer district counterclaimed for an order requiring the property owners to connect their properties to the county-owned sewer system. The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals that voided the ordinance requiring the property owners to connect to the county-owned sewer system because the requirements of due process found in N.C. Const. art. 1, § 19 were met and the ordinance was a valid exercise of the county's police power. The court found that the requiring notice and opportunity for hearing to all individual property owners prior to the adoption of an ordinance mandating connection of improved properties pursuant to the enabling act would be burdensome, costly to local governments, and not consistent with procedures employed in the exercise of other police powers. Specifically, the court held that the law of the land clause does not require notice and opportunity for hearing prior to the passage of an ordinance mandating connection to a sewer system adopted under the authority of N.C. Gen. Stat. § 153A-284.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court off appeals was reversed because the statute and the ordinances pertaining to sewer connection, which were passed without notice and an opportunity to be heard and which mandate connections to the sewer lines as well as the payment of related connection charges and user fees, are consistent with federal procedural due process protections and are a valid exercise of the police power.

State v. Sanders


No. 88A85 - Transylvania


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


327 N.C. 319; 395 S.E.2d 412; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 714


March 9, 1987, Heard in the Supreme Court; December 14, 1988, Reargued  
August 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27, 1 from judgments imposing a sentence of death and a sentence of life imprisonment, entered by Winberry, J., at the 4 February 1985 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Transylvania County. 2


1 At the time of defendant's appeal, N.C.G.S. § 7A-27 permitted appeals directly to this Court from all sentences of death or life imprisonment. The statute was amended in 1987 to permit direct appeals only from first degree murder convictions.


2 Defendant was previously tried and convicted in June 1982 but inaccurate and inadequate transcriptions of these trial proceedings required this Court to vacate the convictions and remand for a new trial. State v. Sanders, 312 N.C. 318, 321 S.E.2d 836 (1984) (per curiam).



DISPOSITION: Case No. 81CRS2879 -- No error. Case No. 81CRS2850 -- No error in guilt proceeding; remanded for a new sentencing proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal Session of Superior Court, Transylvania, North Carolina, which denied his motion to suppress certain evidence in his trial for first degree murder and first degree rape and which imposed a sentence of death and a sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and first degree rape after evidence was taken from his home by a private citizen. During trial, the arresting officer did not testify entirely truthfully. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment and death and filed a motion to suppress the evidence at the sentencing phase of his trial. The motion was denied and defendant appealed. The court affirmed in part and denied in part. The court found no error either in the ruling on his motion to suppress or in the guilt phase of his trial but remanded the case for a new sentencing proceeding. The court held that the denial of defendant's motion to suppress was proper because even if the private citizen had been acting as an agent of the state in visiting defendant's home on a pretense, there was no government involvement in his subsequent actions. The court held that although the officer's testimony was in part false, defendant failed to establish either that it was material or that the prosecution knew it was false and intentionally used it to defendant's prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and denied in part the ruling of the lower court. The court found no error in the guilt proceeding but remanded the case for a new sentencing proceeding.

In re Guess


No. 431PA89 - Wake


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


327 N.C. 46; 393 S.E.2d 833; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 575


April 11, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
July 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31 of the decision of the Court of Appeals, 95 N.C. App. 435, 382 S.E.2d 459 (1989), affirming an order entered by Farmer, J., on 20 May 1987 in Superior Court, Wake County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant North Carolina Board of Medical Examiners sought review of the order of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which affirmed a trial court's determination to reverse and vacate the board's decision to conditionally revoke appellee physician's medical license.


OVERVIEW: Despite the fact that none of a physician's patients had ever been harmed, and some had been helped, the state board of medical examiners charged him with unprofessional conduct pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 90-14(a)(6) based upon his practice of homeopathy. The board revoked his license for as long as he failed to practice conventional medicine. A trial court vacated the board's decision. The court of appeals dismissed for lack of jurisdiction but the court reversed and remanded. On remand, the court of appeals affirmed the trial court's order. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the court of appeals erred in construing § 90-14(a)(6) to add a requirement that each particular practice prohibited by the statute must pose an actual threat of harm as a prerequisite to the board's action. The statute was a valid regulation, which generally tended to secure the public health, safety, and general welfare, and its plain language permitted the board to act against any departure from acceptable medical practice, irrespective of whether or not a patient was injured. The court concluded that the board's decision was supported by competent, material, and substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision in favor of the phsycian.

State v. McCarty


No. 266PA89 - Duplin

326 N.C. 782; 392 S.E.2d 359; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 286


March 12, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review of an unpublished decision of the Court of Appeals, 94 N.C. App. 390, 381 S.E.2d 204 (1989), finding no error in part and granting a new trial in part in a trial before Strickland, J., at the 11 March 1988 Session of Superior Court, Duplin County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded in part. Affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the state sought review of the decision from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which found no error in the admissibility of evidence of other similar sex offenses to show a common scheme or plan by defendant to molest children, but granted defendant a new trial on first degree sexual offense and taking indecent liberties with a child because of an erroneous jury charge.


OVERVIEW: The victim's sister testified that defendant had molested her for nine years during her childhood. The jury was instructed that the testimony was admitted solely to show that defendant had a common plan or scheme as well as the unnatural lust on the alleged commission of the charged crimes. Defendant did not object to the limiting instruction and was convicted. The court of appeals found no error in the admissibility of the testimony but granted a new trial on the charges of first degree sexual offense and taking indecent liberties with a child because of an erroneous jury charge. The state and defendant appealed. The court reversed the decision from the court of appeals that granted a new trial and affirmed the remainder of the decision. The court found that it had held there was no error in a similar jury charge in another matter that involved a conviction for taking indecent liberties with a child. Consequently, there was no error in the charge in defendant's trial for first degree sexual offense or taking indecent liberties with a child. The court held that the testimony of the victim's sister and the limiting instruction in regard to it was not prejudicial error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision from the court of appeals that granted defendant a new trial on the first degree sexual offense and the offense of taking indecent liberties with a child. The court affirmed the court of appeals on all other issues.

Northampton County Drainage Dist. Number One v. Bailey


No. 576A88 - Herford


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 742; 392 S.E.2d 352; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 295


September 11, 1989, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal and discretionary review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, 92 N.C. App. 68, 373 S.E.2d 560 (1988), reversing in part a judgment entered on 6 August 1987 by Phillips, J., in the Superior Court of Hertford County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part, affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners owners appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which reversed in part, and affirmed in part the decision of the trial court in an action filed by plaintiff drainage district against the landowners. The landowners challenged the constitutionality of the appointment of the commissioner's of the drainage district.


OVERVIEW: The landowners challenged the assessments made against them by the drainage district. They claimed that they were deprived of equal protection because the clerk of the court for a county in which the landowners did not reside appointed the commissioners of the drainage district. As such, the landowners could not vote for the clerk who was responsible for appointing the commissioners. The trial court ruled in favor of the landowners; the court of appeals reversed. On further review, the court reversed and held that the landowners were deprived of a fundamental right to vote on equal terms. Moreover, the district did not demonstrate that the classification of voters was necessary to promote a compelling interest. The court concluded that the clerk could have had elected, rather than appointed commissioners. The court further determined that N.C. Gen. Stat. § 156-138.3 violated the law of the land clause of the N.C. Const. insofar as it imposed assessments on landowners within the district without giving them notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court also ruled that the landowners were entitled to recover their attorney fees pursuant to N. C. Gen. Stat. § 6-21(8).


OUTCOME: The court reversed, in part, and affirmed, in part, the decision of the court of appeals in the action filed by the drainage district against the landowners.

State v. Hardison


No. 377A88 - Beaufort


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 646; 392 S.E.2d 364; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 296


November 16, 1989, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment of Griffin (William C.), J., sentencing defendant to life imprisonment upon his conviction of first-degree murder by a jury at the 31 May 1988 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Beaufort County.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Beaufort County (North Carolina), convicting him of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his request for a jury instruction on involuntary manslaughter. The court ruled that where a jury was properly instructed on the elements of first and second degree murder and thereafter returned a verdict of guilty of first degree murder based on premeditation and deliberation it was harmless error not to have instructed on the issue of involuntary manslaughter even where the evidence would have supported such an instruction. Further, the court held that there was no possibility the jurors would have considered the lesser charge even if the instruction had been given because they found him guilty of the greater offense. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that assuming error in not giving a charge on involuntary manslaughter, it was harmless in view of the verdict of first degree murder on the theory of premeditation and deliberation.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was affirmed.

 

195 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Faucette


No. 179A89 - Durham


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 676; 392 S.E.2d 71; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 301


April 9, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
June 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal as of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment of life imprisonment upon defendant's conviction of first-degree murder entered by Allen, J., at the 3 January 1989 Criminal Session of Durham County Superior Court. Defendant's motion to bypass the Court of Appeals with respect to the verdict of guilty of first-degree burglary was allowed on 20 September 1989.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an appeal as of right, N.C. Gen. Stat. § 7A-27(a), from a judgment of life imprisonment upon his conviction by a jury for first-degree murder, with burglary as the underlying felony, in the Durham County Superior Court (North Carolina). Defendant's motion to bypass the court of appeals for the verdict of guilty of burglary was allowed. Defendant was convicted of murdering the mother of his child after breaking into her home.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder under both the theories of premeditation and deliberation and of felony murder, with burglary being the underlying felony. Affirming the conviction and sentence, the court explained that statements the victim made to her son and sister were admissible. The court noted that evidence of the victim's state of mind rebutted defendant's testimony as it pertained to the inference of self-defense, showed that defendant entered the victim's home without consent, and prevented the jury from being misled about why the victim would not allow defendant to visit the home. Noting that only defendant and his victim were likely to have firsthand knowledge of their domestic difficulties, the court ruled that her attorney's recitation of the victim's accounts were the most probative evidence of any available to the state regarding the domestic problems. The court ruled that the use of parts of the indictment to give the jury the bare particulars of the case did not give them a distorted view of the case before them by an initial exposure to the case through the stilted language of indictments and other pleadings.


OUTCOME: Affirming the conviction of first-degree murder and the sentence of life imprisonment, the court ruled that defendant received a fair trial free of prejudicial error.

State v. Bacon


No. 364A87


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 404; 390 S.E.2d 327; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 162


February 12, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right by defendant pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing a death sentence for murder in the first degree entered by Stevens, J., at the 18 May 1987 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Onslow County.



DISPOSITION: Guilt Phase -- no error. Sentencing Phase -- death sentence vacated; remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for murder in the first degree and common law conspiracy to commit murder by the Criminal Session of Superior Court, Onslow County (North Carolina).The jury found that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances for the crimes, and recommended the death sentence for defendant. The trial court sentenced accordingly, adding three years imprisonment for the conspiracy charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to murdering the victim and that the victim's wife, with whom he was living with, wanted to have the victim murdered. The court concluded that defendant received a fair trial free of prejudicial error. However, with respect to defendant's sentencing the court vacated the death sentence and remanded the case to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing because the trial court failed to admit evidence of the mitigating factor that he aided in the apprehension of another felon (the wife), consistent with N.C. Gen. Stat. 15A-2000(f)(8) (1988). Although the trial court's decision not to have portions of the trial recorded as requested by the counsel for defendant pursuant to N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1241 and N.C. Gen. Stat. § 15A-1231(b) might have constituted an error, the court found that defendant failed to show he was prejudiced by the error. The court also ruled that the trial court properly admitted defendant's statements made to the police at his residence on the night of the murder because he was not in custody or under arrest at the time he made the statement, and the statement was not the product of questions or interrogation by the officers.


OUTCOME: The court found no prejudicial error in the guilt phase of defendant's trial, and as such, upheld his conviction for first degree murder and common law conspiracy to commit murder. However, because the court found error in the sentencing phase of defendant's trial, the death sentence was vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court for a new sentencing hearing. The court found no error for the conspiracy sentence.

 

197 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pakulski


No. 407A89


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 434; 390 S.E.2d 129; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 164


March 13, 1990, Heard in the Supreme Court  
April 5, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal by the State of North Carolina pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-30(2) from the decision of a divided panel of the Court of Appeals, 95 N.C. App. 517, 383 S.E.2d 442 (1989), reversing the judgment of Freeman, J., at the 28 March 1988 session of Superior Court, Haywood County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment by the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which reversed defendants' felonious breaking or entering and felonious larceny sentences.


OVERVIEW: In defendants' prior trial, the trial judge arrested judgment on the felonious breaking or entering and felonious larceny charges following a jury verdict of guilty because they constituted the predicate felony for the first-degree murder convictions. Defendants' convictions were reversed in part by the court. At the retrial, the charge of murder in the first degree using armed robbery as the predicate felony ended in a mistrial, and the state prayed for judgment on the felonious breaking or entering and felonious larceny convictions. The court reversed concluding defendants' felonious breaking or entering and felonious larceny sentences were proper because the judgments were arrested only because those offenses formed the offenses upon which the convictions of felony murder were predicated. Once a new trial was ordered on appeal of the felony murder conviction, it was no longer necessary to arrest judgment on the underlying felonies. When the state elected not to pursue the charge of murder in the first degree based on felonious breaking or entering and felonious larceny as the predicate felonies, there was no legal impediment to the imposition of sentences on those convictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, which reversed defendants' felonious breaking or entering and felonious larceny sentences.

 

198 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


River Birch Assoc. v. Raleigh


No. 291PA89


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 100; 388 S.E.2d 538; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 13


October 10, 1989, Heard in the Supreme Court  
February 7, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal by plaintiff and cross-appeal by defendant Homeowners Association of a judgment entered on 8 August 1988 by Brewer, J., sitting without a jury, on the initiative of this Court made ex mero motu pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-31(a) and Rule 15(e)(2) of the Rules of Appellate Procedure to hear the case prior to a determination by the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A North Carolina trial court held that Raleigh, N.C., Raleigh City Code § 10-3073 was a valid exercise of defendant city's authority, which did not constitute a taking against plaintiff developer, and ordered the developer to convey the disputed land to intervenor homeowners' association (association). The developer appealed. The association appealed the exclusion of certain evidence and the denial of individual home owners' intervention.


OVERVIEW: When the developer sought to build on land that was initially set aside as a common area, the city refused to process his application and ordered him to convey the land to the association. On appeal, the court held that the city could order the conveyance pursuant to the ordinance. N.C. Gen. Stat. § 160A-372 permitted the ordinance to provide for the conveyance of the common area when the conveyance was set aside in the approved initial plat and was all that was left to complete the approved project. The ordinance was reasonably related to the purpose of preserving open space and did not constitute a taking. The term "common area" that was contained in the declaration of covenants was a latently ambiguous description of the property. Reference to the preliminary plat and landscaping plat was proper to identify the boundaries of the common area. Individual home owners were proper, but not necessary parties because the association adequately represented their interests. However, the association lacked standing to prosecute claims for fraud and unfair trade practices because the damages would have varied amongst its members and deprived them of an alternative remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that ordered the developer to convey the land to the association, but reversed the decision that denied parol evidence to determine the boundaries of the common area. The court affirmed the denial of individual home owners' intervention and the association's lack of standing. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

199 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


No. 585A87


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 56; 388 S.E.2d 84; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 19


December 14, 1989, Heard in the Supreme Court  
February 7, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Remand of October 3, 1990, Reported at: 1990 N.C. LEXIS 901. Opinion on Remand of June 25, 1992, Reported at: 1992 N.C. LEXIS 405. Opinion on Remand of September 10, 1993, Reported at: 1993 N.C. LEXIS 393. Opinion on Remand of October 6, 1994, Reported at: 1994 N.C. LEXIS 579.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal of right pursuant to N.C.G.S. § 7A-27(a) from a judgment imposing the sentence of death entered by Hobgood, J., at the 8 September 1987 Criminal Session of Superior Court, Person County.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged and convicted of murder in the first degree. The Superior Court, Person County (North Carolina), upon the recommendation of the jury, sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed and raised numerous assignments of error in both the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial.


OVERVIEW: Evidence of defendant's strangulation of another victim was admissible under N.C. R. Evid. 404(b) for the purpose of showing preparation, plan, or knowledge because it was virtually identical prior misconduct that occurred less than three days before the instant offense. The repetition of defendant's photograph and the discrepancy in its size compared to others presented in the pretrial identification procedure was unlikely to have led to the witnesses' misidentification of defendant. Testimony by the victims' parents of their receipt of a collect telephone call from the victim shortly before her death was properly admitted because the parents were able to identify her voice. The submission to the jury of the facts that defendant had previously been convicted of a felony involving the use of violence to the person and that the victim's murder was part of a course of conduct that included the commission of other crimes of violence as aggravating circumstances was supported by the evidence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in requesting the jury to resume its deliberations upon being informed that it was hung after deliberating on the sentence for nearly four hours.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

200 of 1540 DOCUMENTS


Batch v. Chapel Hill


No. 121PA89


SUPREME COURT OF NORTH CAROLINA


326 N.C. 1; 387 S.E.2d 655; 1990 N.C. LEXIS 6


October 10, 1989, Heard in the Supreme Court  
January 18, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On discretionary review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, 92 N.C. App. 601, 376 S.E.2d 22 (1989), affirming in part and reversing in part the order granting summary judgment in favor of the plaintiff entered by Brannon, J., in the Superior Court, Orange County, on 31 December 1987.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town challenged an order from the Court of Appeals (North Carolina), which affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's order granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff land owner in her action disputing defendant's denial of a permit to subdivide her property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff land owner filed an action against defendant town arising from its denial of a permit to subdivide her land. The trial court granted summary judgment to plaintiff. The court of appeals affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that it was error to join the proceeding pursuant to the writ of certiorari with the cause of action alleged in the plaintiff's complaint. As a result, the court considered the questions separately. The court found that the trial court was sitting as a court of appeals when it reviewed the decision of defendant, therefore, it erred in making findings of facts and should have determined if defendant's decision was based upon findings of fact supported by competent evidence and whether such findings supported the conclusion. The evidence on which defendant based its decision was competent, material and substantial, and defendant had authority to require plaintiff to consider future plans. The court reversed the court of appeals and determined that the summary judgment on the issues of plaintiff's complaint were improperly granted because defendant did not improperly deny her permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision, which affirmed in part and reversed in part an order granting summary judgment to plaintiff land owner. The court ruled that it was error to join the writ of certiorari with the plaintiff's complaint. Further, the trial court erred in making findings of fact when it should have determined if defendant town's decision was based on findings of fact supported by competent evidence.
